Razi's Argument Against Influence as a Separate Attribute
Razi argues that if influence were a separate attribute, it would lead to regress.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Razi argues that influence (mu'aththiriyya) cannot be a real attribute separate from the cause and effect, and why this leads to an infinite regress.

Core Idea
Influence cannot be a separate attribute without causing an infinite regress.

Razi continues his critique of causality by examining the possibility that influence is a real attribute distinct from both the cause and the effect. He systematically eliminates all options, showing that whether influence is a substance or an accident, it leads to contradiction or regress. This passage is a powerful example of Ash'ari reasoning against necessary causal connections.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Get the overall flow of the argument before diving into details.
2
Identify the first division: privative vs. positive
Notice how Razi first determines whether influence is privative or positive. He concludes it must be positive because it is the opposite of pure negation.
This establishes that influence is a real attribute, not a mere absence.
3
Follow the second division: substance vs. accident
Razi then asks whether this positive attribute is a substance or an accident. Pay attention to the two reasons against it being a substance.
The two reasons: (1) agency is always an attribute of something, not self-subsistent; (2) if a substance, it would either relate or not, both problematic.
4
Understand the regress argument for accident
If influence is an accident inhering in the cause, it depends on the cause for existence. But then it needs its own cause, leading to infinite regress.
This completes the argument: all possibilities fail.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنما قلنا إنه لا يجوز أن تكون المؤثرية زائدة على ذات المؤثر، وذات الأثر، وذلك لأن على هذا التقدير إما أن تكون المؤثرية أمرًا عدميًا أو ثبوتيًا لا جائز أن تكون عدمياً؛ لأن المؤثرية نقيض اللامؤثرية، واللامؤثرية عدم محض ونفي صرف، وذلك معلوم بالضرورة، وعدم العدم ثبوت، فكانت المؤثرية صفة ثبوتية. ثم نقول: هذه المؤثرية التي هي معلوم ثبوتي وهي مغايرة لذات الأثر وذات المؤثر، إما أن تكون جوهرًا قائما بنفسه، أو عرضًا مفتقرًا إلى موصوف، والأول محال لوجهين: الأول: وهو أن مؤثرية الشيء نعت للشيء وصفة له ولا يمكن تعقلها إلا صفة للشيء ونعتا له فيمتنع أن تكون جوهرا قائما بالنفس. والثاني: أن بتقدير أن تكون جوهرًا قائما بالنفس فهذا الجوهر إما أن يكون بينه وبين الأثر نسبة وإضافة أو لا يكون، فإن كان الأول كان الكلام في تلك النسبة كما في الأول فيلزم التسلسل، وإن كان الثاني فلم يكن بينه وبين الأثر نسبة وإضافة، ولم يكن بينهما تعلق أصلاً، وكان أجنبيًا بالكلية عن ذلك الأثر، ولما بطل هذا القسم تعين أن المؤثرية بتقدير الثبوت وجب أن تكون صفة لذات المؤثر مفتقرة إلى تلك الذات، وكل ما كان مفتقرًا إلى غيره كان ممكنا لذاته مفتقرا في وجوده إلى مؤثر فيلزم افتقار تلك المؤثرية في وجودها إلى موجد آخر وحينئذ يعود الكلام في تأثير المؤثر في وجود تلك المؤثرية، ويلزم التسلسل وهو محال. فثبت بما ذكرنا أنه لو فرض مؤثر يؤثر في أثر لكان تأثيره في ذلك الأثر إما أن يكون نفس المؤثر والأثر، وإما أن يكون مغايرًا لهما، والقسمان باطلان، فكان القول بالتأثير باطلا.
We said that it is not permissible for the agency (mu'aththiriyya) to be additional (za'ida) to the essence of the agent and the essence of the effect, because on this assumption the agency is either something privative (adami) or positive (thubuti). It cannot be privative, because agency is the opposite of non-agency, and non-agency is pure non-existence and absolute negation, and that is known necessarily, and the negation of non-existence is existence, so agency is a positive attribute. Then we say: This agency, which is known as positive and is different from the essence of the effect and the essence of the agent, is either a substance (jawhar) subsisting by itself, or an accident (arad) needing a subject. The first is impossible for two reasons: First: That the agency of a thing is a description and attribute of the thing, and cannot be conceived except as an attribute and description of the thing, so it cannot be a self-subsistent substance. Second: Assuming it is a self-subsistent substance, this substance either has a relation and connection with the effect or it does not. If it does, then the discussion about that relation is as before, leading to regress. If it does not, then there is no relation or connection at all between them, and it is completely alien to that effect. When this division is refuted, it becomes necessary that agency, assuming it is positive, must be an attribute of the essence of the agent, dependent on that essence. And everything that depends on something else is possible by itself and depends for its existence on an agent. Then the dependence of that agency for its existence on another cause follows, and then the discussion returns to the influence of the agent upon the existence of that agency, leading to regress, which is impossible. So it is established by what we have mentioned that if an agent influencing an effect were assumed, its influence upon that effect would either be the very agent and the effect, or be different from both, and both divisions are false. Therefore the statement that there is influence is false.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage completes the Third Question by examining the possibility that influence (mu'aththiriyya) is a real additional attribute (zai'da) distinct from both the cause and the effect. Razi first determines whether such an attribute would be privative (adami) or positive (thubuti). He argues it cannot be privative because it is the opposite of non-agency, which is pure negation; the negation of non-existence is existence, so it is positive. Then he asks whether this positive attribute is a substance (jawhar) or an accident (arad). He gives two reasons against it being a substance: first, agency is inherently a description and attribute of something, not a self-subsistent entity; second, if it were a substance, it would either relate to the effect or not. If it relates, then that relation itself would require further analysis (regress). If it does not relate, then it is entirely disconnected and cannot be the cause of the effect. So it must be an accident inhering in the cause. But if it is an accident, it depends on the cause for its existence, and being dependent, it itself needs an agent to cause it. That agent would then need its own agency, leading to an infinite regress. Therefore, assuming agency as a distinct attribute fails. Thus all possibilities are exhausted: influence is neither identical to cause/effect nor a separate attribute, so the very notion of external influence (ta'thir) is false. This is a powerful argument in the Ash'ari tradition against causality (often aimed at philosophers).

Correction: Razi shows that assuming it as separate leads to regress, so it cannot be separate.

Checkpoint
Why does Razi conclude that agency cannot be a substance?

B) Because agency is always an attribute of something, not a self-standing entity
C) Because substances cannot cause anything

Key Takeaway
Razi's argument shows that influence cannot be a real attribute separate from the cause and effect without leading to an infinite regress, thus undermining the notion of necessary causal connection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you credit a person, a medicine, or a natural process for bringing about a result, do you genuinely believe they have independent causal power? How does Razi's argument—that any such influence would require an infinite regress—challenge your default assumption? Will you now consciously remind yourself that only God is the true agent?
?
If you truly internalised that there is no real influence in creation, how would your reliance on material means change? Would your fear of people's harm or hope in their benefit diminish? Set one concrete intention today to shift your trust from secondary causes to the Creator alone.
?
You routinely say 'this caused that' without a second thought. After this lesson, what specific habit or phrase will you change to avoid attributing real causal power to created things? Write down one practical commitment you will act on within the next 24 hours.

The Causal Property Must Be an Existent Attribute
Razi argues that causal property is distinct from essence and effect, and must be existent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the causal property (al-mu'thiriyya) cannot be identified with the agent's essence or effect, and why it must be an existent attribute.

Core Idea
The causal property cannot be pure non-existence; it must be a real existent attribute.

Imam al-Razi begins his fourth argument by clarifying that we do not attribute the effect to the agent's essence, but to its being an agent. He then refutes the idea that the causal property is merely the agent's essence or the effect. The key move is to show that the causal property cannot be a non-existent thing, because it is the opposite of non-agent-property, which is pure negation. Thus, the causal property is necessarily an existent attribute.

Guided Path
1
Understanding the basic distinction
Read the opening where Razi distinguishes between attributing the effect to the agent's essence versus to its being an agent. Notice he says we say 'because Allah created it', not 'because Allah is existent'. This sets up the problem.
This distinction is crucial: the causal property is not the essence itself.
2
Why the causal property cannot be identical to the agent or effect
Razi gives several arguments that the causal property is not the same as the agent's essence or the effect. The truth of negation and affirmation requires differentiation. Make sure you follow this reasoning.
3
Proving causal property is existent
Now Razi argues that the causal property (mu'thiriyya) cannot be 'adami (non-existent) because it is the opposite of non-agent-property, which is pure non-existence. The non-existence of non-existence is existence, so mu'thiriyya is thubūtī (existent).
This step uses the law of non-contradiction in a simple way.
4
Connecting to the next lesson
Having established that mu'thiriyya is an existent attribute, the next question is whether it is a substance or an accident. That will be taken up in the next lesson.
You have now set the stage for the deeper analysis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع : وهو أنا نعلل الأثر بذات المؤثر، بل بكونه مؤثراً، فإنا نقول: إنما وجد هذا الأثر لأن الباري تعالى أوجده وأبدعه وخلقه، ولا نقول: إنما وجد هذا الأثر لأن الباري تعالیٰ موجود وواجب الوجود، وصدق النفي والإثبات يوجب التغاير. فبطل بهذه الوجوه أن يقال كون المؤثر مؤثرًا في الشيء عبارة عن ذات المؤثر، وذات الأثر، وإنما قلنا إنه لا يجوز أن تكون المؤثرية زائدة على ذات المؤثر، وذات الأثر، وذلك لأن على هذا التقدير إما أن تكون المؤثرية أمرًا عدميًا أو ثبوتيًا لا جائز أن تكون عدمياً ؛ لأن المؤثرية نقيض اللامؤثرية، واللامؤثرية عدم محض ونفي صرف، وذلك معلوم بالضرورة، وعدم العدم ثبوت، فكانت المؤثرية صفة ثبوتية. ثم نقول : هذه المؤثرية التي هي معلوم ثبوتي وهي مغايرة لذات الأثر وذات المؤثر، إما أن تكون جوهرًا قائما بنفسه، أو عرضًا مفتقرًا إلى موصوف، والأول محال لوجهين : الأول : وهو أن مؤثرية الشيء نعت للشيء وصفة له ولا يمكن تعقلها إلا صفة للشيء ونعتا له فيمتنع أن تكون جوهرا قائما بالنفس. والثاني : أن بتقدير أن تكون جوهرًا قائما بالنفس فهذا الجوهر إما أن يكون بينه وبين الأثر نسبة وإضافة أو لا يكون، فإن كان الأول كان الكلام في تلك النسبة كما في الأول فيلزم التسلسل، وإن كان الثاني فلم يكن بينه وبين الأثر نسبة وإضافة، ولم يكن بينهما تعلق أصلاً، وكان أجنبيًا بالكلية عن ذلك الأثر، ولما بطل هذا القسم تعين أن المؤثرية بتقدير الثبوت وجب أن تكون صفة لذات المؤثر مفتقرة إلى تلك الذات، وكل ما كان مفتقرًا إلى غيره كان ممكنا لذاته مفتقرا في وجوده إلى مؤثر فيلزم افتقار تلك المؤثرية في وجودها إلى موجد آخر وحينئذ يعود الكلام في تأثير المؤثر في وجود تلك المؤثرية، ويلزم التسلسل وهو محال. فثبت بما ذكرنا أنه لو فرض مؤثر يؤثر في أثر لكان تأثيره في ذلك الأثر إما أن يكون نفس المؤثر والأثر، وإما أن يكون مغايرًا لهما، والقسمان باطلان، فكان القول بالتأثير باطلا.
The Fourth: And it is that we do not attribute the effect to the essence of the agent, but rather to its being an agent. For we say: This effect exists only because the Exalted Creator brought it into existence, originated it, and created it. And we do not say: This effect exists only because the Exalted Creator exists and is the Necessary Existent. And the truth of negation and affirmation necessitates differentiation. So it is invalidated by these arguments that it is said that the agent's being an agent in the thing is an expression of the agent's essence and the effect's essence. And we only said that it is not permissible for the agent-property (al-mu'thiriyya) to be additional to the agent's essence and the effect's essence. That is because, on this assumption, either the agent-property is a non-existent thing (amr 'adami) or an existent thing (thubūtī). It cannot be non-existent because the agent-property is the opposite of non-agent-property, and non-agent-property is pure non-existence and sheer negation, and that is known necessarily, and the non-existence of non-existence is existence, so the agent-property is an attribute of existence. Then we say: This agent-property, which is known as existent and is distinct from the effect's essence and the agent's essence, is either a substance (jawhar) subsisting by itself or an accident ('araḍ) dependent on a subject. The first is impossible for two reasons: First: because the agent-property of a thing is a description (na't) and attribute (ṣifa) of the thing, and it cannot be conceived except as an attribute and description of the thing, so it cannot be a substance subsisting by itself. Second: if we suppose it to be a substance subsisting by itself, then this substance either has a relation (nisba) and connection (iḍāfa) to the effect or not. If the first, then the discussion applies to that relation as in the first [case], leading to infinite regress. If the second, then there is no relation and connection between it and the effect, and no attachment at all, and it would be completely foreign to that effect. And when this division is invalidated, it is determined that the agent-property, on the assumption of its existence, must be an attribute of the agent's essence dependent on that essence. And everything dependent on another is possible by itself and dependent in its existence on an agent. So the dependence of that agent-property in its existence on another originator would be necessary, and then the discussion returns to the agent's effect on the existence of that agent-property, and infinite regress follows, which is impossible. So it is established by what we have mentioned that if an agent is supposed to have an effect, its effect on that effect would be either identical to the agent and the effect or distinct from them both, and both divisions are invalid, so the statement of [real] effect is invalid.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is a fourth argument (or objection) aiming to refute the reality of causal effect. The author argues that the causal property (being an agent) cannot be a real additional attribute distinct from the agent's essence and the effect's essence. He first distinguishes between attributing the effect to the agent's essence versus to its being an agent. He then argues that if the agent-property were additional, it would have to be either non-existent or existent. It cannot be non-existent because it is the opposite of non-agent-property, which is pure negation. So it must be existent. Then he examines whether it is a substance or an accident. It cannot be a substance because it is a description, and if it were a substance, it would either relate to the effect or not, leading to infinite regress or complete disconnection. Hence it must be an accident dependent on the agent, but then it would itself need an agent, leading to infinite regress. Therefore the notion of a real causal effect is false.

Misconception: Some might think that the causal property is identical to the agent's essence.
Correction: Razi argues that effects are not attributed to the essence but to the attribute of being an agent, and truth of negation/affirmation shows they are distinct.

Checkpoint

A) Because non-existence cannot be a cause.
B) Because the causal property is the opposite of non-agent-property, which is pure non-existence, and the non-existence of non-existence is existence.
C) Because non-existence is impossible.

Key Takeaway
The causal property (al-mu'thiriyya) must be an existent attribute, distinct from the agent's essence and the effect.

?
The passage refutes the idea that non-existence can explain anything. Are there areas in your life where you treat spiritual neglect or absence—like 'I just don't pray'—as an acceptable state, as if non-action is neutral? How will you replace this emptiness with a positive act of obedience today?
?

Do you sometimes reduce your relationship with Allah to a set of automatic outcomes (e.g., 'If I pray, I get reward') instead of engaging with Him as a Personal Agent who responds to your specific situation? Causality and Created Things
advanced

Why the Causal Property Leads to Infinite Regress
Razi examines substance/accident alternatives for causal property and shows both lead to absurdity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a real causal property (mu'thiriyya) cannot be a substance or an accident without leading to infinite regress.

Core Idea
If causal property is a real attribute, it either is a substance (impossible) or an accident (leading to infinite regress).

In this second part of the fourth argument, Imam al-Razi examines what kind of existent the causal property could be. He argues it cannot be a substance because it is a description and because it would either relate to the effect (leading to regress) or be disconnected (absurd). The only remaining option is that it is an accident dependent on the agent, but then it itself would need an agent, leading to infinite regress. Hence, the notion of a real causal effect is invalid.

Guided Path
1
The substance/accident division
Read where Razi says the causal property must be either jawhar (substance) or 'arad (accident). Pay attention to the two arguments against it being a substance.
A substance in kalam is something that subsists by itself, like a body or atom.
2
Why it cannot be a substance
First reason: a causal property is a description (na't) and attribute, and cannot be conceived except as an attribute of something. So it cannot be self-subsisting. Second reason: if it were a substance, it would either have a relation to the effect or not. If relation, then the same discussion applies to that relation, leading to infinite regress. If no relation, it would be entirely foreign and could not be a cause.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
3
Why it cannot be an accident either
If it is an accident dependent on the agent, then it is possible in itself and needs an agent for its existence. That agent would need its own causal property, leading to infinite regress. So the assumption of a real causal property leads to impossibility.
This is the classic infinite regress argument (tasalsul).
4
Final conclusion
Razi concludes that the notion of a real causal effect (ta'thir) is invalid because whether causal property is identical to agent/effect or distinct, both are impossible.
This does not deny that effects occur; it denies that there is a real attribute of 'being a cause' distinct from the agent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع : وهو أنا نعلل الأثر بذات المؤثر، بل بكونه مؤثراً، فإنا نقول: إنما وجد هذا الأثر لأن الباري تعالى أوجده وأبدعه وخلقه، ولا نقول: إنما وجد هذا الأثر لأن الباري تعالیٰ موجود وواجب الوجود، وصدق النفي والإثبات يوجب التغاير. فبطل بهذه الوجوه أن يقال كون المؤثر مؤثرًا في الشيء عبارة عن ذات المؤثر، وذات الأثر، وإنما قلنا إنه لا يجوز أن تكون المؤثرية زائدة على ذات المؤثر، وذات الأثر، وذلك لأن على هذا التقدير إما أن تكون المؤثرية أمرًا عدميًا أو ثبوتيًا لا جائز أن تكون عدمياً ؛ لأن المؤثرية نقيض اللامؤثرية، واللامؤثرية عدم محض ونفي صرف، وذلك معلوم بالضرورة، وعدم العدم ثبوت، فكانت المؤثرية صفة ثبوتية. ثم نقول : هذه المؤثرية التي هي معلوم ثبوتي وهي مغايرة لذات الأثر وذات المؤثر، إما أن تكون جوهرًا قائما بنفسه، أو عرضًا مفتقرًا إلى موصوف، والأول محال لوجهين : الأول : وهو أن مؤثرية الشيء نعت للشيء وصفة له ولا يمكن تعقلها إلا صفة للشيء ونعتا له فيمتنع أن تكون جوهرا قائما بالنفس. والثاني : أن بتقدير أن تكون جوهرًا قائما بالنفس فهذا الجوهر إما أن يكون بينه وبين الأثر نسبة وإضافة أو لا يكون، فإن كان الأول كان الكلام في تلك النسبة كما في الأول فيلزم التسلسل، وإن كان الثاني فلم يكن بينه وبين الأثر نسبة وإضافة، ولم يكن بينهما تعلق أصلاً، وكان أجنبيًا بالكلية عن ذلك الأثر، ولما بطل هذا القسم تعين أن المؤثرية بتقدير الثبوت وجب أن تكون صفة لذات المؤثر مفتقرة إلى تلك الذات، وكل ما كان مفتقرًا إلى غيره كان ممكنا لذاته مفتقرا في وجوده إلى مؤثر فيلزم افتقار تلك المؤثرية في وجودها إلى موجد آخر وحينئذ يعود الكلام في تأثير المؤثر في وجود تلك المؤثرية، ويلزم التسلسل وهو محال. فثبت بما ذكرنا أنه لو فرض مؤثر يؤثر في أثر لكان تأثيره في ذلك الأثر إما أن يكون نفس المؤثر والأثر، وإما أن يكون مغايرًا لهما، والقسمان باطلان، فكان القول بالتأثير باطلا.

Causality and Created Things

The Fourth Objection: Symmetry of Existence and Non-Existence
Razi states the fourth objection as a reductio argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourth objection to the argument from possibility, which uses a symmetry reductio to challenge the need for a cause.

Core Idea
If possibility requires a cause for existence, it would also require a cause for non-existence – which is impossible.

This lesson presents a crucial objection to the kalam argument that possibility necessitates a creator. The objection uses a symmetry argument: if possibility is a ground for needing a cause, then both existence and non-existence would equally need causes. But non-existence, being pure absence, cannot have a cause. This reductio ad absurdum challenges the very foundation of the argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Notice the structure: it is a reductio argument that starts with a premise and derives a contradiction.
The passage is short but dense. Focus on the logical flow.
2
Identify the symmetry premise
The objection assumes that possibility of existence applies equally to existence and non-existence. Find the line that states 'جواز الوجود متعلق بالطرفين' (possibility of existence pertains to both sides).
This is the key assumption that drives the reductio.
3
Understand the reductio logic
Trace the argument: if possibility of existence → need for cause, then by analogy possibility of non-existence → need for cause. But non-existence cannot need a cause (because it is pure negation and eternal), so the original implication must be false.
The conclusion is that the argument from possibility is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السؤال الرابع: إن جواز الوجود متعلق بالطرفين أعني الوجود والعدم فلو كان جواز الوجود يقتضي احتياج الوجود إلى المؤثر لكان جواز العدم يقتضي احتياج العدم إلى المؤثر، لكن احتياج العدم إلى المؤثر محال ؛ لأن العدم نفي محض وسلب صرف، فجعله أثرًا أو مؤثرًا محال ؛ ولأن العدم مستمر من الأزل إلى الأبد، والباقي لا يمكن إسناد حال بقائه إلى المؤثر. فثبت أنه لو كان جواز الوجود يحوج الوجود إلى المؤثر لكان جواز العدم يحوج العدم إلى المؤثر ، فثبت أن احتياج العدم إلى المؤثر محال، فيلزم أن يكون احتياج الوجود أيضًا إلى المؤثر محالا.
The Fourth Question: Indeed, possibility of existence pertains to both sides, namely existence and non-existence. So if possibility of existence required existence's need for an agent, then possibility of non-existence would require non-existence's need for an agent. But non-existence's need for an agent is impossible, because non-existence is pure negation and sheer privation, so making it an effect or an agent is impossible; and because non-existence is continuous from eternity to eternity, and the persistent cannot have its state of persistence attributed to an agent. So it is established that if possibility of existence makes existence need an agent, then possibility of non-existence would make non-existence need an agent. Then it is established that non-existence's need for an agent is impossible, so it follows that existence's need for an agent is also impossible.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This is a fourth objection against the argument that possibility necessitates a creator. It points out a symmetry between existence and non-existence: if possibility of existence required a cause for existence, then by the same reasoning possibility of non-existence would require a cause for non-existence. But non-existence is pure absence, so it cannot have a cause. Therefore, the original premise (that possibility is a ground for needing a cause for existence) is false.

Key Terms
جواز الوجود
جواز العدم
مؤثر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The objection claims that non-existence actually needs a cause.
Correction: No, the objection is a reductio: it shows that if the premise were true, it would lead to the absurd conclusion that non-existence needs a cause, so the premise must be false.

Checkpoint
What is the flaw in the argument that possibility requires a cause for existence, according to the fourth objection?
A) It ignores the possibility of non-existence.
B) It would also require a cause for non-existence, which is impossible.
C) Non-existence is continuous from eternity.
D) Existence and non-existence are symmetrical.

Key Takeaway
The fourth objection uses symmetry to show that the argument from possibility is self-defeating.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you present arguments for God's existence, do you ever consider that your reasoning might be flawed in ways you haven't noticed? How does Razi's objection challenge your confidence in rational proofs?
?
Razi uses a logical trick to show a contradiction. Have you ever defended a belief with an argument that, upon reflection, leads to an absurdity? What did you do?
?
If the argument from possibility is not valid, what does that mean for your personal conviction about the necessity of a Creator? Does your faith rest on intellectual proofs or on something deeper?

The Fifth Question: Need for Agent During Persistence
The fifth objection argues that if possibility were the cause of need, things would need an agent even while persisting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the argument that possibility necessitates a creator is challenged by the problem of persistence, and how the objection of 'attaining the already-attained' refutes it.

Core Idea
If possibility caused need, things would need a creator even while existing – which is absurd.

This lesson presents the fifth objection against the claim that possibility (al-imkan) is the cause of a thing's need for an agent. The objection raises a powerful logical problem: if possibility were truly the cause, then things would need an agent not only at origination but also throughout their persistence, leading to an unintelligible repetition of creation. The passage then examines and refutes a series of counterarguments, ultimately concluding that possibility cannot be the cause.

Guided Path
1
Read the objector's argument
Read the passage carefully. Notice the main claim: if possibility were the cause of need, then persisting things would need an agent. This is argued by noting that possibility is a constant concomitant of possible essences.
The key term here is 'تحصيل الحاصل' (attaining the already-attained).
2
Understand the entailment
The objector shows that possibility is always present with possible things. So if possibility causes need, need must also be constant, which is absurd because it would require the effect to be produced again.
3
Examine the first counter-reply
The objector anticipates a reply: that during persistence, the agent's influence is on persistence, not the essence. The author rejects this because persistence is additional to the essence, so influencing persistence is not influencing the essence. But the essence itself is still possible in the second moment.
4
Reject the condition of originatedness
Another attempt to rescue the claim is to add the condition of originatedness (ḥudūth) to possibility. The author quickly dismisses this, citing an earlier proof that originatedness cannot be a cause, part, or condition for need.
5
Conclude the argument
The passage ends with a firm conclusion: possibility is not the cause of need. This sets the stage for the correct view, which will be explored in subsequent lessons.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السؤال الخامس : لو كان الجواز علة للحاجة إلى المؤثر لكان الشيء حال بقائه مفتقرًا إلى المؤثر، وهذا محال، فالقول بأن الجواز علة للحاجة إلى المؤثر محال بيان الملازمة هو أن الإمكان من لوازم الماهيات الممكنة، ولازم الشيء حاصل في جميع زمان وجوده ، وكان الإمكان حاصلا حال بقاء الممكنات، فلو كان الإمكان علة للحاجة إلى المؤثر لزم افتقار الباقي حال بقائه إلى المؤثر، وإنما قلنا : إن هذا محال لأن هذا يقتضي تحصيل الحاصل وهو محال. يقال : لم لا يجوز أن يكون تأثير المؤثر حال بقاء الأثر في بقائه، وبقاؤه لا زائد على ذاته؟ لأنا نقول : بقاؤه لما كان زائدا على ذاته لم يكن التأثير في بقائه تأثيرا في ذاته، لكنا بينا أن ذاته من حيث هي هي ممكنة في الزمان الثاني فلو كان الإمكان علة للحاجة إلى المؤثر لكانت ذاته من حيث هي هي محتاجة في الزمان الثاني إلى المؤثر، وذلك محال ؛ لأنه يقتضي تحصيل الحاصل وتكوين الكائن وهو غير معقول، فوجب القطع بأن الإمكان ليس علة للحاجة إلى المؤثر. لا يقال : لم لا يجوز أن يقال : الإمكان علة للحاجة إلى المؤثر بشرط الحدوث، وهذا الشرط غير حاصل حال البقاء، فلم يلزم تحقق الاحتياج حال البقاء؟ لأنا نقول : إنا بينا في ما تقدم أن الحدوث لا يمكن أن يكون علة للحاجة ولا جزءًا لهذه العلة ولا شرطا لها فسقط قولكم.
The Fifth Question: If possibility were the cause of the need for an agent, then a thing while persisting would be in need of an agent. This is impossible. So the statement that possibility is the cause of the need for an agent is impossible. The explanation of the entailment is that possibility is among the necessary concomitants (lawāzim) of possible essences, and the concomitant of a thing obtains throughout the entire time of its existence, and possibility obtains during the persistence of possibles. So if possibility were the cause of the need for an agent, the persistent would be in need of an agent during its persistence. And we say: This is impossible because it would necessitate attaining the already-attained (taḥṣīl al-ḥāṣil), which is impossible. It is said: Why is it not permissible that the influence of the agent during the persistence of the effect is on its persistence, and its persistence is not additional to its essence? We say: Since its persistence is additional to its essence, the influence on its persistence is not an influence on its essence. But we have shown that its essence in itself is possible in the second moment. So if possibility were the cause of the need for an agent, then its essence in itself would be in need of an agent in the second moment, and that is impossible because it would necessitate attaining the already-attained and bringing about the already-existing (takwīn al-kā'in), which is unintelligible. So it is necessary to conclude that possibility is not the cause of the need for an agent. It cannot be said: Why is it not permissible to say that possibility is the cause of the need for an agent only with the condition of originatedness (ḥudūth), and this condition is not present during persistence, so the need is not realized during persistence? We say: We have shown earlier that originatedness cannot be a cause for need, nor a part of this cause, nor a condition for it, so your statement falls.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This is the fifth objection against the argument that possibility requires a creator. It argues that if possibility were the cause of need for an agent, then the thing would need an agent even after it exists, but that is absurd because it would be repeating the effect (taḥṣīl al-ḥāṣil). The objection considers a counter-argument: that the agent's influence during persistence is on persistence, not on the essence, and that persistence is not additional. The author responds that persistence is additional, so influencing persistence is not influencing the essence, but the essence is still possible in the second moment and would need an agent again. Another counter-argument regarding the condition of originatedness is also refuted because originatedness cannot be a condition for need.

Key Terms
الإمكان
البقاء
حدوث
شرط
تحصيل الحاصل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the objection only applies to the moment of origination, but the argument shows it applies to persistence as well because possibility is always present.
Correction: The objection explicitly targets persistence: if possibility causes need, then because possibility remains, need remains, leading to the absurdity of repeatedly creating what already exists.

Checkpoint
What is the main argument of the fifth objection?
A) Possibility is not a cause for need.
B) If possibility were a cause, things would need an agent during persistence.
C) Persistent entities do not need agents.
D) The condition of originatedness solves the problem.

Key Takeaway
Possibility cannot be the cause of need for an agent because it would entail an absurd regress of creation during persistence.

?

?
How can you, right now, make your heart feel the weight of depending on God for your persistence, and not just your origination?

The Sixth Question: Refuting the Eternal Agent for Observed Events
Razi begins the sixth objection with an argument against an eternal agent for observed events.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first half of the sixth objection: why an eternal agent cannot be the cause of observed originated events because its influence would require an originated condition, leading to an infinite regress.

Core Idea
An eternal agent cannot cause originated events without an originated condition, causing a regress.

In this objection, Razi argues that if we assume observed events need an agent, that agent cannot be eternal. The reason is that if an eternal agent's influence depends on an originated condition, then that condition itself needs an agent, leading to an infinite chain. This is a crucial argument against the possibility of an eternal cause for temporal effects.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: the objection states a conditional argument against the eternal agent.
The passage is incomplete; the part against the originated agent is missing.
2
Identify the key terms
Focus on 'حدوث' (origination), 'قدم' (eternity), and 'شرط حادث' (originated condition). These are central to the argument.
3
Understand the conditional argument
The passage presents a disjunction: the eternal agent's influence is either conditional on an originated condition or not. If conditional, then the condition is also originated and would need its own agent, leading to regress.
The passage cuts off before discussing the case where it is not conditional.
4
Recognize the regress problem
If the condition is originated, it must have an agent, and that agent would again face the same issue, leading to infinite regress. This refutes the possibility of an eternal agent.
This is a classic argument against an eternal cause for temporal effects.
5
Note the incompleteness
The text ends abruptly. The full objection also includes an argument against an originated agent, but it is not present here. This lesson covers only the part against the eternal agent.

Source Text

السؤال السادس : لا شك أنا نشاهد حدوث صور وأعراض في هذا العالم، فلو كان الحدوث والإمكان علة للحاجة إلى المؤثر فيها فالمؤثر فيها إما أن يكون قديمًا أو حادثاً، والقسمان باطلان فبطل القول بالمؤثر، وإنما قلنا إنه لا يجوز أن يكون المؤثر فيها قديما ؛ لأن تأثير ذلك المؤثر القديم فيها إما أن يكون موقوفا على شرط حادث أو لا يكون كذلك، فإن كان الأول عاد التقسيم الأول فيه فيلزم أن
The Sixth Question: There is no doubt that we observe the origination of forms and accidents in this world. So if origination and possibility are the cause of the need for an agent in them, then the agent in them must be either eternal (qadīm) or originated (ḥādith). Both divisions are invalid, so the statement of an agent is invalid. And we only say that it is not permissible for the agent in them to be eternal because the influence of that eternal agent on them is either conditional on an originated condition or not. If the first, then the first division returns in it, leading to...

This is the sixth objection, arguing that observed originated events cannot have an agent because the agent must be either eternal or originated. If eternal, its influence would require an originated condition, leading to infinite regress; if originated, it would itself need an agent. The text is cut off but the argument is clear in its presented part: the agent cannot be eternal because its influence would depend on an originated condition, which leads to a regress. The rest of the argument (the case of an originated agent) is not fully present in this window.

Fifth Objection: Possibility as Cause of Need for Efficient Cause
Imam Razi presents and refutes the fifth objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Razi's refutation of the fifth objection against possibility being the cause of need for an efficient cause.

Core Idea
Possibility cannot cause need for a cause because it would lead to absurd repetition.

In this lesson, we examine the fifth objection to the claim that possibility (al-imkan) is the cause of need for an efficient cause. The objector argues that if possibility were the cause, then a thing would need a cause even during its persistence, which is absurd. Imam Razi refutes this by showing the logical consequences and rejecting attempts to limit the need to origination.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and its demonstration
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Identify the main objection: that if possibility causes need, then persistence would also require a cause, which is impossible.
Notice that the objector first states the entailment and then declares it impossible.
2
Understand the implication of persistence
Focus on the demonstration: possibility is a concomitant of all possible essences, present at all times. Therefore, if it were the cause of need, need would persist, leading to the absurdity of 'tahsil al-hasil' (acquiring what is already acquired).
3
Analyze the sub-objections
Examine the two sub-objections raised: (1) that the efficient cause's effect could be in persistence itself, and (2) that need is conditional on origination. Understand how each tries to avoid the absurdity.
Razi rejects both: persistence is additional to essence, so effect in persistence is not effect in essence; and origination cannot be a condition for need.
4
Evaluate the refutations
See how Razi systematically refutes each sub-objection, concluding that possibility is not the cause of need for an efficient cause. Reflect on the strength of the argument.
The refutation relies on the principle that the essence in the second moment is possible and thus would still need a cause, which is absurd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السؤال الخامس : لو كان الجواز علة للحاجة إلى المؤثر لكان الشيء حال بقائه مفتقرًا إلى المؤثر، وهذا محال، فالقول بأن الجواز علة للحاجة إلى المؤثر محال بيان الملازمة هو أن الإمكان من لوازم الماهيات الممكنة، ولازم الشيء حاصل في جميع زمان وجوده ، وكان الإمكان حاصلا حال بقاء الممكنات، فلو كان الإمكان علة للحاجة إلى المؤثر لزم افتقار الباقي حال بقائه إلى المؤثر، وإنما قلنا : إن هذا محال لأن هذا يقتضي تحصيل الحاصل وهو محال. يقال : لم لا يجوز أن يكون تأثير المؤثر حال بقاء الأثر في بقائه، وبقاؤه لا زائد على ذاته؟ لأنا نقول : بقاؤه لما كان زائدا على ذاته لم يكن التأثير في بقائه تأثيرا في ذاته، لكنا بينا أن ذاته من حيث هي هي ممكنة في الزمان الثاني فلو كان الإمكان علة للحاجة إلى المؤثر لكانت ذاته من حيث هي هي محتاجة في الزمان اللثاني إلى المؤثر، وذلك محال ؛ لأنه يقتضي تحصيل الحاصل وتكوين الكائن وهو غير معقول، فوجب القطع بأن الإمكان ليس علة للحاجة إلى المؤثر. لا يقال : لم لا يجوز أن يقال : الإمكان علة للحاجة إلى المؤثر بشرط الحدوث، وهذا الشرط غير حاصل حال البقاء، فلم يلزم تحقق الاحتياج حال البقاء؟ لأنا نقول : إنا بينا في ما تقدم أن الحدوث لا يمكن أن يكون علة للحاجة ولا جزءًا لهذه العلة ولا شرطا لها فسقط قولكم.
The fifth question: If possibility were the cause of the need for the efficient cause, then the thing during its state of persistence would be in need of the efficient cause, and this is impossible. So the statement that possibility is the cause of the need for the efficient cause is impossible. The demonstration of the entailment is that possibility is among the concomitants of possible essences, and the concomitant of a thing is present in all the time of its existence. Possibility is present during the state of persistence of possibles. So if possibility were the cause of the need for the efficient cause, then the persistence of the remaining [thing] in its state of persistence would necessitate need for the efficient cause. And we say: this is impossible because it requires the acquisition of the acquired, which is impossible. It is said: Why is it not permissible that the effect of the efficient cause during the state of persistence of the effect be in its persistence, and its persistence is not additional to its essence? We say: Since its persistence is additional to its essence, the effect in its persistence is not an effect in its essence. But we have shown that its essence, considered in itself, is possible in the second moment. So if possibility were the cause of need for the efficient cause, then its essence, considered in itself, would be in need of the efficient cause in the second moment, and that is impossible because it requires the acquisition of the acquired and the bringing into existence of the existent, which is unintelligible. So it must be conclusively stated that possibility is not the cause of need for the efficient cause. It is not said: Why is it not permissible to say that possibility is the cause of need for the efficient cause on the condition of origination, and this condition is not present during the state of persistence, so the realization of need during the state of persistence does not follow? We say: We have shown in what has preceded that origination cannot be a cause for need, nor a part of this cause, nor a condition for it. So your statement collapses.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes the fifth objection against the claim that possibility (al-imkan) is the cause of need for an efficient cause (al-mu'aththir). The objection argues that if possibility were the cause, then a thing would need the efficient cause even during its state of persistence (hal al-baqa'), which is absurd because it would require the repetition of the effect (tahsil al-hasil). The objector then raises a sub-objection: why can't the efficient cause's effect be in the persistence itself, if persistence is not additional? The author responds that persistence is indeed additional, so effect in persistence is not effect in essence. Then he reiterates that the essence in the second moment is possible and would still need a cause, leading to absurdity. Another sub-objection suggests that need could be conditional on origination (al-huduth), which is absent during persistence. The author responds that he has already proven that origination cannot be a cause, part, or condition for need. Thus the objection fails.

Key Terms
الجواز
الإمكان
المؤثر
الاحتياج
الحدوث
البقاء
تحصيل الحاصل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Possibility causes need only at origination, not during persistence.
Correction: Imam Razi argues that origination cannot be a cause, part, or condition for need, so this conditional view is invalid. The need, if caused by possibility, would persist.

Checkpoint

A) Because persistence is not additional to essence.
B) Because it would require the acquisition of the acquired (tahsil al-hasil).
C) Because the efficient cause only acts at origination.
D) Because possibility ceases during persistence.

Key Takeaway
Imam Razi conclusively refutes the fifth objection by showing that possibility cannot be the cause of need for an efficient cause, as it would lead to absurdities like acquiring the acquired.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Examine your heart: do you only turn to Allah when something new happens, or do you recognize your constant need for Him in every breath? Commit today to acknowledging His continuous sustenance by thanking Him not just for beginnings, but for every moment.
?
The objection suggests that need is only at origination, but Razi refutes this. Do you treat your relationship with Allah as if you only needed Him at the start of your faith, but now you are self-sufficient? In what areas of your life have you stopped relying on Him, thinking you have 'arrived'? This lesson calls you to repent from the illusion of independence and to cry out to Allah in every second, knowing that without His constant care, you would cease to exist.
?
Razi shows that 'tahsil al-hasil'—trying to acquire what is already acquired—is absurd. Yet, do you not often strive to earn what Allah has already given you: His mercy, His guidance, His provision? Are you trying to 'earn' His love as if it were not freely given? Let this truth break your pride: you cannot add to what He has already bestowed. Instead, accept His gifts with gratitude and cease the exhausting effort of trying to secure what is already secured.

Sixth Objection: Observed Origination Undermines the Need for a Cause
Razi's sixth objection arguing observed origination disproves the need for an efficient cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the sixth objection argues that observed origination disproves the necessity of an efficient cause by showing both possibilities (eternal or originated cause) lead to contradictions.

Core Idea
Observed origination cannot prove a cause; both eternal and originated causes fail.

In this passage, Imam Razi presents a powerful objection against the standard Ash'ari argument that origination (huduth) necessitates an efficient cause. The objector argues that from our observation of things coming into existence, we cannot logically deduce a cause, because positing either an eternal or an originated cause leads to absurdities. This objection targets the very foundation of the cosmological argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully. Note the structure: the objector starts with an observed fact, then divides possibilities, and argues each leads to a problem.
2
Identify the two branches
The objection splits the possible efficient cause into two categories: eternal (qadim) and originated (hadith). Pay attention to how each is refuted.
The eternal cause branch has two subcases.
3
Analyze the subcases for the eternal cause
For the eternal cause, the effect must either depend on an originated condition or not. If it does, infinite regress follows; if not, the event's timing is arbitrary. Understand why both are considered unacceptable.
Infinite regress (tasalsul) and arbitrary specification are key concepts.
4
Consider the originated cause branch
The objector argues that if the cause is originated, the same argument applies to that cause, leading again to infinite regress or a simultaneous infinite chain, which contradicts the idea of a Necessary Existence.
This reinforces the overall conclusion that the efficient cause claim is false.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السؤال السادس : لا شك أنا نشاهد حدوث صور وأعراض في هذا العالم، فلو كان الحدوث والإمكان علة للحاجة إلى المؤثر فيها فالمؤثر فيها إما أن يكون قديمًا أو حادثاً، والقسمان باطلان فبطل القول بالمؤثر، وإنما قلنا إنه لا يجوز أن يكون المؤثر فيها قديما ؛ لأن تأثير ذلك المؤثر القديم فيها إما أن يكون موقوفا على شرط حادث أو لا يكون كذلك، فإن كان الأول عاد التقسيم الأول فيه فيلزم أن يكون حدوث ذلك الشرط الحادث لأجل حدوث شرط آخر، ولزم التسلسل، وإن كان الثاني لزم اختصاص حدوث هذا الحادث بهذا الوقت دون ما قبله لا لأمر أصلا البتة، فكان هذا قولا بوقوع الجائز، لا عن سبب ولا عن مرجح، وهذا يبطل القول بافتقار الجائز إلى المرجح. وإنما قلنا : إنه لا يجوز أن يكون المؤثر في حدوث هذه الحوادث في هذا الوقت أمرًا حادثا لأن الكلام يعود فيه، ويلزم التسلسل، وحصول أسباب ومسببات لا نهاية لها دفعة واحدة وذلك يبطل القول بإثبات واجب الجود.
The sixth question: There is no doubt that we observe the origination of forms and accidents in this world. So if origination and possibility were the cause of need for the efficient cause in them, then the efficient cause in them must be either eternal or originated. Both divisions are false, so the statement of the efficient cause is false. We say: It is not permissible that the efficient cause in them be eternal, because the effect of that eternal efficient cause in them must either be dependent on an originated condition or not be so. If the first, then the first division recurs in it, and thus the origination of that originated condition would be due to the origination of another condition, and infinite regress (tasalsul) would follow. If the second, then the specification of this originated event to this time rather than before would follow without any reason at all. So this would be a statement of the occurrence of the possible without a cause or without a preponderator, and this falsifies the statement that the possible is in need of a preponderator. And we say: It is not permissible that the efficient cause in the origination of these events at this time be an originated thing, because the argument would recur in it, and infinite regress would follow, and the occurrence of an infinite number of causes and effects at once, and that falsifies the statement of affirming a Necessary Existence (Wajib al-Jud).
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage presents the sixth objection against the claim that origination (al-huduth) and possibility (al-imkan) are causes of need for an efficient cause. The objector argues from observed origination: we see forms and accidents originate. If origination and possibility necessitate a cause, then that cause must be either eternal (qadim) or originated (hadith). Both are argued to be impossible. If the cause is eternal, its effect either depends on an originated condition or not. If it does, an infinite regress results. If it does not, then the event's specification to a particular time is arbitrary, undermining the need for a cause (murajjih). If the cause is originated, the same argument applies to it, leading to infinite regress or simultaneous infinite causes, which negates the proof of a Necessary Existence. Thus the objector claims the notion of an efficient cause is falsified.

الإمكان

المرجح
واجب الجود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The objection denies causality entirely.
Correction: It only denies that origination/possibility are the grounds for needing a cause, not causality per se.

Checkpoint
According to the sixth objection, what follows if the eternal efficient cause's effect is not dependent on an originated condition?
A) The event would occur necessarily.
B) Infinite regress would follow.
C) The event's occurrence at a specific time would be arbitrary and without cause.
D) The cause would be originated.

Key Takeaway
The sixth objection uses infinite regress and arbitrary specification to argue that observed origination does not prove the need for an efficient cause.

?

?
This objection argues that without a condition, an eternal cause would act arbitrarily. In your own life, do you sometimes assume that because something is possible, it must have a clear cause? How can this passage push you to deepen your trust in Allah as the ultimate preponderator, even when you cannot trace the reasons?
?
If the argument from origination fails to prove a cause, have you ever felt your faith shaken by philosophical objections? What in this lesson can help you strengthen your conviction that Allah is the Necessary Existence, beyond the arguments that human reason alone can construct?

The Seventh Objection: Totality of Events Cannot Have an Efficient Cause
Imam Razi presents the seventh objection: the totality of temporal events cannot have an efficient cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Razi's seventh objection challenges the necessity of an efficient cause for temporal events by considering the totality of events and showing the impossibility of both an originated and an eternal cause.

Core Idea
The totality of originated events cannot have an efficient cause without absurdity.

In this passage, Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi presents a powerful dialectical objection to the claim that every originated event requires an efficient cause. He focuses on the totality of events occurring at a given moment and shows that whether one posits an efficient cause or not, difficulties arise. The objection is structured as a dilemma, systematically eliminating each possibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and English translation to get the flow of the argument. Notice the logical connectors like 'either...or' and 'impossible'.
This is a dense logical text; reading slowly helps.
2
Identify the main dilemma
The argument splits into two main cases: the totality either has an efficient cause or not. Then the first case splits further into originated or eternal cause.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum structure.
3
Understand why an originated cause is impossible
The objection argues that if the cause were originated, it would be part of the totality, causing a self-causation problem—the cause cannot be separate from its effect.
Key point: cause must be distinct from effect.
4
Understand why an eternal cause is impossible
If the cause is eternal, its causality is a new attribute (mujidiyya) that began at the time of causation. This new attribute itself would need a cause, leading to circularity or infinite regress.
This challenges the theistic claim directly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السؤال السابع : وهو أن نقول : جملة ما حدث في هذا الوقت إما أن يكون له مؤثر أو لا يكون، فإن لم يكن له مؤثر فقد حدث الحادث لا عن مؤثر، وذلك يبطل القول بافتقار الممكن والمحدث إلى المؤثر، وأما إن كان لها مؤثر فالمؤثر فيها إما إن يكون حادثا أو قديما، ويمتنع أن يكون حادثًا لأن المؤثر في الشيء مغاير للأثر، فلو كان المؤثر في جملة الحوادث حادثاً لكان ذلك الحادث مغايرا لجملة الحوادث، وذلك محال ؛ لأن كل ما كان حادثا كان داخلا في جملة الحوادث وفي مجموعها. ويمتنع أن يكون المؤثر فيها قديمًا لأن ذلك القديم قبل إيجاده هذه الحوادث لم يكن موجدًا لها ولا مخرجًا لها من العدم إلى الوجود، والآن صار موجدا لها ومخرجًا لها من العدم إلى الوجود، فتكون موجدية الموجد لها حكمًا متجدداً، وحينئذ يعود ما ذكرنا من تعليل جملة الحوادث لشيء حادث، وذلك محال على ما بيناه. وأيضًا فلو افتقر الحادث إلى المؤثر لافتقرت هذه الموجدية الحادثة إلى المؤثر، فيلزم إما الدور وإما التسلسل، وهما محالان وبتقدير القول بهما يبطل الطريق إلى إثبات الصانع، وإذا كان كذلك وجب أن تكون تلك الموجدية المتجددة غنية عن المؤثر، وذلك يوجب القطع باستغناء الممكن المحدث عن المؤثر.
The seventh question: It is that we say: The totality of what occurs at this time either has an efficient cause or does not have one. If it does not have an efficient cause, then the occurred event occurs without an efficient cause, and that falsifies the statement that the possible and the originated are in need of an efficient cause. And if it has an efficient cause, then the efficient cause in them must be either originated or eternal. It is impossible that it be originated, because the efficient cause of a thing is other than the effect. So if the efficient cause of the totality of events were originated, then that originated thing would be other than the totality of events, and that is impossible, because everything that is originated is included in the totality of events and in its sum. And it is impossible that the efficient cause in them be eternal, because that eternal [being], before it brought these events into existence, was not a bringer-into-existence of them nor an extricator of them from non-existence to existence, and now it has become a bringer-into-existence of them and an extricator of them from non-existence to existence. So the bringing-into-existence (mujidiyya) of the bringer-into-existence of them is a renewed attribute. Then what we have mentioned regarding the attribution of the totality of events to an originated thing recurs, and that is impossible as we have shown. Moreover, if the originated were in need of the efficient cause, then this originated bringing-into-existence would be in need of an efficient cause, and then either circularity (al-dawr) or infinite regress (al-tasalsul) would follow, and both are impossible. And upon the supposition of accepting them, the way to affirm the Maker (al-Sani') would be falsified. If it is as such, then that renewed bringing-into-existence must be independent of the efficient cause, and that necessitates the conclusive statement that the possible originated thing is independent of the efficient cause.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage presents the seventh objection against the need for an efficient cause for originated events. The objection considers the totality of events occurring at a given time. It either has an efficient cause or not. If not, the claim that the possible/originated needs a cause is false. If yes, the cause is either originated or eternal. An originated cause is impossible because any originated thing is part of the totality, so it cannot cause the totality (it would be both cause and effect). An eternal cause is impossible because before causing, it was not a cause, and its causality is a new attribute, which would itself need a cause, leading to circularity or infinite regress. Therefore, the originated must be independent of a cause, contradicting the original claim.

Key Terms
جملة الحوادث
المؤثر
الحادث
القديم
الموجدية
الدور
التسلسل
الصانع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The objection claims that the efficient cause must be part of the totality of events.
Correction: It argues that an originated cause, if it exists, would necessarily be part of the totality because every originated thing is included, making it impossible for it to be the cause of the whole.

Checkpoint
Why does the seventh objection consider it impossible for the efficient cause of the totality of events to be originated?
A) Because the originated is included in the totality, so it would be both cause and effect.
B) Because an originated cause would lead to infinite regress.
C) Because the originated cause would be eternal.
D) Because the originated cause would be independent of the totality.

Key Takeaway
The seventh objection challenges the necessity of an efficient cause by showing that whether the totality of events has a cause (originated or eternal) or not, absurdity follows.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In this objection, Razi argues that if the totality of events has no cause, then events occur without purpose. Do you live your life as if everything happens by random chance, forgetting that Allah is the ultimate cause of all things? What would change if you truly internalized that every moment is under His control?
?
The objection shows that finite minds can fall into apparent dilemmas about causality. When you encounter a difficulty in understanding Allah's actions, do you humbly submit that His wisdom is beyond yours, or do you let your intellect lead you to doubt? What step can you take today to surrender your reasoning to His revelation?
?
The conclusion of this objection is that the possible originated thing is independent of an efficient cause. But you know that you are utterly dependent on Allah. Are there areas of your life—your health, wealth, or relationships—where you act as if you are self-sufficient? How can you acknowledge your need for Him in those areas right now?

Answer to the First Objection: Simultaneity of Cause and Effect
Imam Razi answers the first objection regarding the timing of the efficient cause's effect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi refutes the objection that simultaneous causation leads to 'bringing the existent into existence' by distinguishing between a pre-existing thing and a newly originated thing.

Core Idea
Simultaneous causation does not bring an already existing thing into existence again.

Imam Razi addresses a key objection: if the cause's effect is simultaneous with existence, wouldn't that involve the absurdity of bringing an already existing thing into existence? He clarifies that the objection confuses two different cases. This passage shows his precise distinction that saves the doctrine of causality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its English translation. Notice the flow: the objector's statement, then Razi's answer.
The answer is concise but logically tight.
2
Identify the objector's claim
The objector says that simultaneous causation implies 'bringing a existent into existence' (ijad al-mawjud), which he claims is impossible. Underline that part.
3
Examine Razi's distinction
Razi breaks the concept of 'bringing into existence' into two cases: (1) bringing an existent that already existed before the act (impossible), and (2) bringing an existent that did not exist before but comes to be at the moment of the act (not impossible). Count how many times he uses 'إيجاد'.
The key is the phrase 'ما كان موجودًا قبل ذلك الإيجاد' vs 'ما لم يكن موجودًا قبل ذلك الإيجاد'.
4
Reflect on why this matters
Consider why the objector's confusion could undermine the entire argument for causality. Razi's distinction preserves the normal understanding of origination from nothing.
This is a classic example of clarifying terms in theological debates.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب عن السؤال الأول : لم لا يجوز أن يقال : تأثير المؤثر في الوجود مع الوجود لا قبله ولا بعده ؟ وقول السائل : " هذا يقتضي إيجاد الموجود يحصل وهو محال " . فجوابه أن إيجاد موجود كان موجودًا قبل ذلك الإيجاد محال، وإنما إيجاد موجود ما كان موجودًا قبل ذلك الإيجاد وإنما حصل حال ذلك الإيجاد فلم قلتم بأنه محال ؟
And the answer to the first question: Why is it not permissible to say: The effect of the efficient cause on existence is simultaneous with existence, not before it nor after it? And the statement of the questioner: 'This necessitates bringing the existent into existence, which is impossible.' So its answer is that bringing into existence an existent that existed before that bringing into existence is impossible. But bringing into existence an existent that did not exist before that bringing into existence, and only came to be at the moment of that bringing into existence — why do you say it is impossible?
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage provides the answer to the first objection (presented earlier). The objector had argued that if the efficient cause's effect is simultaneous with existence, it would be 'bringing the existent into existence' (ijad al-mawjud), which is absurd. The author refutes this by distinguishing between an existent that already existed before the act (which would indeed be absurd to bring into existence again) and an existent that did not exist before but comes into existence at the very moment of the act. The latter is precisely what is meant by origination, and it is not absurd. Therefore, the objection fails.

Key Terms
تأثير المؤثر
الوجود
إيجاد الموجود
الإيجاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That 'bringing the existent into existence' always means repeating an already existing thing.
Correction: Imam Razi clarifies that it can also mean bringing a nonexistent into existence at the moment of causation, which is not absurd.

Checkpoint
In the answer to the first objection, what does Imam Razi argue about bringing an existent into existence?
A) It is always impossible.
B) It is possible if the existent existed before the act.
C) It is possible if the existent did not exist before the act but comes to be at the moment of the act.
D) It is possible only if the cause is eternal.

Key Takeaway
Simultaneous causation does not involve bringing into existence something that already exists; it is the origination of something from nonexistence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

The Impossibility of Infinite Regress in Temporal Causation
Imam Razi argues against infinite regress in the causation of temporal events.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why an infinite regress of temporal causes is rationally impossible and how it undermines the proof of a Necessary Being.

Core Idea
Infinite regress in causation is rationally impossible; it leads to absurdity and destroys the foundation for a Necessary Being.

Imam Razi presents a powerful logical argument against the possibility of an infinite chain of temporal causes. He shows that any attempt to explain the occurrence of temporal events through other temporal events leads either to an infinite regress or to causeless events, both of which are rationally unacceptable. This passage establishes the necessity of a First Cause that is not itself temporal.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's argument flow naturally before you dissect it.
The argument is dense; read slowly.
2
Identify the two alternatives
The passage presents two possible explanations for why a temporal event occurs at a specific time. Find both and note how each leads to a problem.
3
Understand the consequences
Understand why each alternative is problematic: the first leads to infinite regress, the second violates causality. Then grasp the conclusion that the cause cannot be temporal.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يكون حدوث ذلك الشرط الحادث لأجل حدوث شرط آخر، ولزم التسلسل، وإن كان الثاني لزم اختصاص حدوث هذا الحادث بهذا الوقت دون ما قبله لا لأمر أصلا البتة، فكان هذا قولا بوقوع الجائز، لا عن سبب ولا عن مرجح، وهذا يبطل القول بافتقار الجائز إلى المرجح.
وإنما قلنا : إنه لا يجوز أن يكون المؤثر في حدوث هذه الحوادث في هذا الوقت أمرًا حادثا لأن الكلام يعود فيه، ويلزم التسلسل، وحصول أسباب ومسببات لا نهاية لها دفعة واحدة وذلك يبطل القول بإثبات واجب الجود.
If the occurrence of that conditioned event occurs due to another condition, then infinite regress (تسلسل) follows; and if the second [alternative] entails the specification of the occurrence of this event at this time rather than before it without any reason at all, then this is a statement of the occurrence of the possible (جائز) without a cause (سبب) and without a preponderator (مرجح), and this invalidates the claim that the possible requires a preponderator. And we say: It is not permissible that the effecting entity (مؤثر) in the occurrence of these events at this time be a temporal thing, because the same argument would apply to it, leading to infinite regress, and the simultaneous occurrence of causes and effects without end, and that invalidates the proof for establishing the Necessary Being (واجب الجود).
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is an argument against the possibility of an infinite regress of causes for temporal events. The author presents two alternatives: either the event is caused by a prior condition, leading to an infinite chain, or it occurs at a specific time without any cause, which contradicts the principle that every possible thing requires a preponderator. He then argues that the cause cannot be temporal itself, because that would lead to infinite regress and undermine the proof of a Necessary Existent. The argument is structured as a reductio ad absurdum, showing that accepting an infinite regress destroys the rational foundation for establishing the existence of a necessary being.

Key Terms
التسلسل
المرجح
المؤثر
واجب الوجود
الجائز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Infinite regress of causes is possible.
Correction: Imam Razi shows it leads to logical absurdity and invalidates the proof for a Necessary Being.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Razi, what logical consequence follows if one posits a temporal event as the cause of other temporal events?
A) The argument ends at the First Cause
B) Infinite regress occurs
C) The cause is eternal
D) The effect is unnecessary

Key Takeaway
Infinite regress in temporal causation is rationally impossible; the only coherent explanation requires a non-temporal First Cause.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If infinite regress is impossible, then every moment in your life is directly caused by the Necessary Being. Do you truly live with that awareness, or do you sometimes act as if your circumstances are random and purposeless?
?
The argument shows that without a non-temporal cause, events would happen without reason. Are there areas of your life where you have accepted 'no reason' for your trials or blessings, rather than turning to God as the ultimate Preponderator?
?
Imam Razi's proof destroys the possibility of an endless chain of causes. Does your trust in God reflect this truth, or do you silently believe that your struggles are an endless cycle without a final, meaningful resolution in Him?

Answering the Objection on Simultaneous Causation
Imam Razi responds to the objection that simultaneous causation implies creating an already existing thing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi refutes the objection that simultaneous causation entails causing an already existing thing, by distinguishing between bringing something into existence that already existed and bringing something into existence at the very moment.

Core Idea
Simultaneous causation creates new existence, not duplicate existence.

Imam Razi addresses a critical objection to the Ash'ari view of creation: if the cause produces its effect at the same moment, doesn't that mean creating something that already exists? In this passage, he clarifies the distinction between impossible repetition and instantaneous creation, defending the coherence of simultaneous causation.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage once and its translation. Identify the objector's claim and Imam Razi's response.
The objector says simultaneous causation implies 'إيجاد الموجود' (bringing into existence something existing).
2
Identify the central distinction
Notice how Imam Razi distinguishes between two types of 'إيجاد': one that brings into existence something that already existed (impossible) and one that brings into existence something that did not exist before but comes to be at that moment (possible).
This distinction is the key to the answer.
3
Understand why the objection fails
The objector conflates the two types. Imam Razi shows that simultaneous causation only involves the second type, so the charge of impossibility is invalid.
The effect is new, not pre-existing.
4
Reflect on the broader implications
Consider how this defense upholds the Ash'ari view that creation is instantaneous and that causation occurs at the same moment as the effect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب عن السؤال الأول : لم لا يجوز أن يقال : تأثير المؤثر في الوجود مع الوجود لا قبله ولا بعده ؟ وقول السائل : " هذا يقتضي إيجاد الموجود يحصل وهو محال " . فجوابه أن إيجاد موجود كان موجودًا قبل ذلك الإيجاد محال، وإنما إيجاد موجود ما كان موجودًا قبل ذلك الإيجاد وإنما حصل حال ذلك الإيجاد فلم قلتم بأنه محال ؟
The answer to the first question: Why is it not permissible to say: The effect of the effecting entity (تأثير المؤثر) is in conjunction with existence (مع الوجود), not before it nor after it? And the questioner's statement: 'This entails bringing into existence (إيجاد الموجود) something existing, which is impossible.' So the answer is that bringing into existence something that existed before that bringing into existence is impossible; rather, bringing into existence something that did not exist before that bringing into existence, but only comes into existence (حصل) at the moment of that bringing into existence — why do you say it is impossible?
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a response to an objection about simultaneous causation. The objector claims that if a cause brings about its effect at the same moment, it would mean creating something already existent, which is absurd. Imam Razi refutes this by distinguishing between bringing into existence something that already existed (which is indeed impossible) and bringing into existence something that did not exist before but comes into existence exactly at the moment of causation. The latter is precisely what creation ex nihilo means, so there is no absurdity.

Key Terms
تأثير المؤثر
إيجاد الموجود
حصول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If a cause produces an effect at the same time, it means causing something that already existed, which is absurd.
Correction: Imam Razi shows that causing something that did not exist before but comes into existence at the moment of causation is not absurd; it is the only way to understand creation.

Checkpoint
How does Imam Razi respond to the objection that simultaneous causation implies bringing an already existing thing into existence?
A) He admits it is impossible
B) He says the effect existed before causation
C) He distinguishes between causing something that existed before and causing something new at that moment
D) He denies simultaneous causation

Key Takeaway
Simultaneous causation does not cause an already existing thing; it brings about a new existence at that precise moment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider that God creates everything in your life—your next breath, your next thought—at the very moment it occurs, without any gap or delay, does that make you more aware of your absolute dependence on Him? How does this conviction change the way you plan your day or react to unexpected events?
?
The objector in this passage insists that either the cause precedes the effect or it is nonsense. Are there areas in your faith where you have accepted similar false dichotomies—forcing God's actions into human temporal categories? What would it mean for you to surrender that need for control and accept God's creative act as simultaneous with existence?
?
If your very existence at this moment is a direct result of God's will right now—not a continuation from the past—then what does that say about your past sins? Are you still defined by them, or do you see yourself as a new creation each moment? How can this truth free you from despair over past failures and motivate you to turn to God in repentance now?
