Refuting the Tripartite Division of Renewal
Imam Razi refutes an objection dividing renewal into three categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi refutes an objection dividing renewal into three categories by showing each leads to absurdity, and how this demonstrates the invalidity of the objection.

Core Idea
The division of renewal into essence, existence, or attribute creates contradictions that make renewal impossible.

Imam Razi now turns to a second objection that tries to undermine the argument for causality by analyzing renewal into three categories. He shows that this very division, if taken seriously, would prevent any renewal from happening at all — which is absurd because we clearly see things renew. In this passage, he systematically refutes each category, revealing the logical flaws.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the objection's division
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice that the objector divides renewal into three possibilities: essence, existence, or the attribute of essence with existence.
The division is introduced in the sentence starting with ' وإما '.
2
Understand the refutation of essence renewal
Razi argues that renewing essence would mean something changing into itself (e.g., blackness becoming blackness), which is a contradiction.
This is a clear logical absurdity.
3
Follow the refutation of existence renewal
Similarly, renewing existence would mean existence becoming existence, again a self-change of essence.
The same logic applies.
4
Analyze the refutation of the third category
The attribute of essence with existence either is not an extra thing (so cannot be renewed) or is extra, leading back to the same division.
This traps the objector in a dilemma.
5
See the conclusion: division contradicts observed renewal
Razi concludes that the division makes renewal impossible, but we observe renewal, so the division is false.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب عن السؤال الثاني : أنه لو وقعت الشكوك والشبهات في تأثير شيء في شيء لامتنع تجدد شيء وحدوثه، لكنه لا شك ولا شبهة في تجدد الحوادث والصور والأعراض، وما ذكرتموه من التقسيم ههنا بعينه، وذلك لأنه لو تجدد أمر أو حدث أمر لكان المتجدد إما الماهية أو الوجود أو موصوفية الماهية بالوجود والكل محال، فوجب أن لا يحصل التجدد أصلا. وإنما قلنا إنه يمتنع تجدد الماهية لأنه يلزم أن يقال : السواد ما كان سوادًا ثم انقلب سواداً، وذلك يقتضي انقلاب الماهية والحقيقة، وذلك محال. وإنما قلنا : إنه يمتنع تجدد الوجود لأنه يقتضي أن يقال : الوجود ما كان وجودًا ثم انقلب وجودًا، وذلك يقتضي انقلاب الماهية. وإنما قلنا : إنه يمتنع تجدد موصوفية الماهية بالوجود لأن هذه الموصوفية إن لم تكن أمرًا زائدا على الماهية وعلى الوجود امتنع القول بأنها المتجددة، وإن كانت أمرًا زائدا فالمتجدد إما ماهيتها أو وجودها ويعود التقسيم المذكور. فثبت أن ما ذكرتم من التقسيم يمنع من القول بالتجدد والحدوث، ولما كان ذلك مشاهدًا محسوسًا علمنا أن ما ذكرتم من التقسيم باطل.
The answer to the second question: If doubts and ambiguities occurred regarding the causality of one thing for another, then no renewal (تجدد) or occurrence would be possible; but there is no doubt or ambiguity in the renewal of events, forms, and accidents. And the division (تقسيم) you have mentioned here is exactly the same. Because if something were renewed or occurred, the renewed entity would be either the essence (ماهية), or existence (وجود), or the attribute of the essence with existence (موصوفية الماهية بالوجود) — and all are impossible. Thus, no renewal would occur at all. We say that the renewal of essence is impossible because it would necessitate saying: blackness was not blackness, then it turned into blackness, which entails a change of essence and reality, and that is impossible. We say that the renewal of existence is impossible because it would necessitate saying: existence was not existence, then it turned into existence, which entails a change of essence. We say that the renewal of the attribute of essence with existence is impossible because if that attribute is not an extra thing over the essence and over existence, then it cannot be said to be renewed; if it is an extra thing, then what is renewed is either its essence or its existence, and the same division applies. Thus, the division you mentioned prevents the affirmation of renewal and occurrence. Since renewal is observed and sensed, we know that the division you mentioned is false.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection that proposes a tripartite division of what is renewed: essence, existence, or the attribute of essence with existence. Imam Razi shows that each of these leads to absurdities. Renewal of essence would mean something changing into itself (e.g., blackness becoming blackness). Renewal of existence would similarly be self-contradictory. The third option (attribute) either is not distinct from essence and existence, so cannot be renewed, or is distinct, leading back to the same division. Thus the division makes renewal impossible, contradicting empirical observation, so the division is false.

الماهية

الموصوفية
التقسيم

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that renewal can be meaningfully analyzed into three categories (essence, existence, attribute).
Correction: Imam Razi shows that each category leads to a logical impossibility, so the division itself is invalid.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Razi, what is the flaw in the objector's division of renewal into essence, existence, or the attribute of essence with existence?
A) It is incomplete
B) It leads to contradictions such as essence changing into itself
C) It is based on sense perception
D) It only applies to blackness

Key Takeaway
Imam Razi demonstrates that the objector's tripartite division of renewal is self-defeating because each branch leads to a logical impossibility, which contradicts the evident reality of change.

Refuting the Division of Occurrence: Essence or Accident?
Imam Razi refutes the division that occurrence is either identical to essence or additional to it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Razi rejects the dichotomy that occurrence is either identical to essence or additional to it, and grasp the three rational arguments against identity.

Core Idea
Occurrence is a relation, not the essence itself.

Imam Razi continues his defense of the doctrine of creation by addressing an objection that reduces occurrence to a binary: either it is the essence itself or an addition. In this passage, he argues both options are rationally impossible, providing three proofs against identity and starting the refutation of addition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without overanalyzing. Then read the literal translation. Pay attention to the logical flow of the objection and its refutation.
The text ends mid-sentence; we cover only this part.
2
Identify the objection and the two alternatives
Notice that the objection divides occurrence into being either identical to the essence (ذات) or additional (زائد). Understand why this is a false dichotomy.
This is the core of the third objection being answered.
3
Analyze the three arguments against identity
Imam Razi gives three distinct reasons: (1) conceivability of essence without occurrence, (2) occurrence is a relation distinct from essence, (3) if identical, essences would perish in the next hour. Work through each.
These are self-contained rational proofs.
4
Observe the beginning of the argument against addition
The passage starts refuting the second alternative by noting that any added element would itself be an occurrence, leading to a regress. The argument is cut off but the direction is clear.
This shows the systematic refutation of both horns.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب عن السؤال الثالث: أن ذلك التقسيم أيضًا قائم فيما عرف فساده بالضرورة، وذلك لأنه يقال : لو حصل شيء في هذه الساعة لكان حصوله في هذه الساعة إما أن يكون حصوله نفس ذاته أو زائدا على ذاته والقسمان باطلان، فبطل القول بحصوله في هذه الساعة وإنما قلنا : إنه لا يجوز أن يكون حصول هذه السماء وحصول هذه الأرض في هذه الساعة نفس ذات السماء ونفس ذات الأرض لوجوه. أحدها: أنه يمكننا أن نعقل ذات السماء وذات الأرض مع الشك مع حصولهما في هذه الساعة. والثاني : أن حصولهما في هذه الساعة نسبة لتينك الذاتين إلى هذه الساعة، والنسبة بين الشيئين مغايرة لهما. والثالث : أن ذات السماء والأرض لو كانتا نفس حصولهما في هذه الساعة ففي الساعة الثانية لم يبق حصولهما في الساعة الأولى، فوجب أن لا تبقى ذاتهما في الساعة الثانية، فإن التزموا ذلك وقالوا : الأجسام تحدث حالا بعد حال الزمناهم في واجب الوجود، وإنما قلنا : إنه لا يجوز أن يكون حصول السماء والأرض في هذه الساعة زائدا على الذات لأن ذلك الزائد يكون حاصلا لا محالة في هذه الساعة،
The answer to the third question: That same division also applies to what is known to be false by necessity. Because it is said: If something occurs in this hour, then its occurrence in this hour is either identical to its essence (ذات) or additional (زائد) to its essence — both are false. So the statement of its occurrence in this hour becomes invalid. And we say: It is not permissible that the occurrence of this heaven and this earth in this hour be identical to the essence of heaven and the essence of earth, for several reasons. One: We can conceive of the essence of heaven and earth while doubting their occurrence in this hour. Two: Their occurrence in this hour is a relation (نسبة) of those two essences to this hour, and the relation between two things is distinct (مغايرة) from them. Three: If the essence of heaven and earth were identical to their occurrence in this hour, then in the second hour their occurrence in the first hour would no longer be, so their essences would have to cease in the second hour. If they accept that and say bodies are created moment by moment, we would lead them to [the Necessary Being]. And we say: It is not permissible that the occurrence of heaven and earth in this hour be additional to the essence, because that additional thing would necessarily occur in this hour, [and the argument continues].
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage is a response to an objection that posits a dichotomy: occurrence in a given time is either identical to the essence or additional to it. Imam Razi argues that both alternatives are false. He provides three reasons why occurrence cannot be identical to essence: (1) we can conceive of the essence without its temporal occurrence, (2) occurrence is a relation distinct from the essence, and (3) if identical, then when the occurrence changes, the essence would change, leading to moment-by-moment creation, which would force one into affirming the Necessary Being. He then begins to argue against the second alternative (occurrence as additional), but the text is cut off. The passage shows the rational refutation of a false dichotomy.

النسبة
المغايرة

Misconception: Occurrence must be either the essence itself or an additional attribute like color or shape.
Correction: Imam Razi shows both alternatives lead to contradictions; occurrence is actually a relation between essence and time, not a property of the essence.

Checkpoint

A) We can conceive of essence without its occurrence in that hour

Key Takeaway
Occurrence is a relation between essence and time, not identical to essence nor a superadded accident; both alternatives are rationally impossible.

Answer to the Second Objection: Refutation of the Impossibility of Renewal
Imam Razi refutes an objection that renewal (tajaddud) is impossible through a divisive argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi refutes the objection that renewal (tajaddud) is impossible by using the opponent's own logical division.

Core Idea
A flawed division cannot negate directly observed reality.

Imam Razi now addresses the second objection, which claims that renewal (tajaddud) is impossible because the renewed thing must be either the essence, existence, or the qualification of essence by existence, all supposedly impossible. Instead of offering a separate proof for renewal, Razi turns the division against the objector. He shows that if the division were valid, it would deny the evident fact of change in the world. Since renewal is directly perceived, the division that would negate it must be false.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice that Razi is responding to an objection, not presenting a new argument.
The objection uses a logical division (taqsim) to argue that renewal is impossible.
2
Trace Razi's refutation strategy
Identify how Razi turns the division against the objector. He argues that if the division were correct, then no change would ever occur, which contradicts direct observation.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum.
3
Examine the three branches
Look at the three possibilities for the renewed thing: essence, existence, or the qualification of essence by existence. Understand why Razi claims each is impossible under the opponent's assumptions.
Pay attention to the reasoning for each branch, especially the third one where the opponent's division reapplies.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Razi concludes that since renewal is observed, the division is false. Ask yourself how this argument fits into the larger discussion of causality and divine attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب عن السؤال الثاني : أنه لو وقعت الشكوك والشبهات في تأثير شيء في شيء لامتنع تجدد شيء وحدوثه، لكنه لا شك ولا شبهة في تجدد الحوادث والصور والأعراض، وما ذكرتموه من التقسيم ههنا بعينه، وذلك لأنه لو تجدد أمر أو حدث أمر لكان المتجدد إما الماهية أو الوجود أو موصوفية الماهية بالوالكل محال، فوجب أن لا يحصل التجدد أصلا. وإنما قلنا إنه يمتنع تجدد الماهية لأنه يلزم أن يقال : السواد ما كان سوادًا ثم انقلب سواداً، وذلك يقتضي انقلاب الماهية والحقيقة، وذلك محال. وإنما قلنا : إنه يمتنع تجدد الوجود لأنه يقتضي أن يقال : الوجود ما كان وجودًا ثم انقلب وجودًا، وذلك يقتضي انقلاب الماهية. وإنما قلنا : إنه يمتنع تجدد موصوفية الماهية بالوجود لأن هذه الموصوفية إن لم تكن أمرًا زائدا على الماهية وعلى الوجود امتنع القول بأنها المتجددة، وإن كان أمرًا زائدا فالمتجدد إما ماهيتها أو وجودها ويعود التقسيم المذكور. فثبت أن ما ذكرتم من التقسيم يمنع من القول بالتجدد والحدوث، ولما كان ذلك مشاهدًا محسوسًا علمنا أن ما ذكرتم من التقسيم باطل.
The answer to the second question: If doubts and obscurities occurred concerning the influence of one thing upon another, then the renewal and origination of anything would be impossible. But there is no doubt or obscurity concerning the renewal of events, forms, and accidents. And that very division which you have mentioned here is [applicable], because if an affair renews or an event occurs, the renewed thing is either the essence (mahiyya), or existence (wujud), or the qualification of the essence by existence, and all [of these] are impossible, so renewal should not occur at all. We say that the renewal of the essence is impossible because it would necessitate saying: 'Blackness was not blackness and then turned into blackness,' which necessitates the change of essence and reality, and that is impossible. We say that the renewal of existence is impossible because it would necessitate saying: 'Existence was not existence and then turned into existence,' which necessitates change of essence. We say that the renewal of the qualification of the essence by existence is impossible because this qualification, if it is not an extra thing over the essence and over existence, then it is impossible to say that it is the renewed thing; and if it is an extra thing, then the renewed is either its essence or its existence, and the division returns. Thus it is established that the division you have mentioned prevents the affirmation of renewal and origination, and since that [renewal] is witnessed and perceived, we know that the division you have mentioned is false.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage is an answer to the second objection. Imam Razi argues that if one denies causal influence, then renewal (tajaddud) would be impossible. The objector used a division (taqsim) to argue that renewal is impossible because the renewed thing must be either essence (mahiyya) or existence (wujud) or the qualification of essence by existence, all purportedly impossible. Razi turns the argument: this same division, if applied consistently, would deny the evident reality of change in the world. Since renewal is directly observed, the division that leads to its denial must be false. He then explains each branch: renewing the essence would mean blackness becoming blackness, which is a change of essence (impossible); renewing existence would mean existence becoming existence, also a change of essence; and the qualification, if not extra, is nothing new, and if extra, falls into the same division. Thus the opponent's own reasoning is self-defeating.

ماهية
وجود
موصوفية
انقلاب
تقسيم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This argument is a denial of change
Correction: It is actually a refutation of a flawed logical division that would deny change, using the opponent's own reasoning.

Checkpoint

B) Because it leads to the denial of observable renewal and change.
C) Because it assumes essences can change.
D) Because it requires an infinite regress.

Key Takeaway
Imam Razi defeats the objection by showing that the same division used to deny renewal would also deny the obvious fact of change in the world, proving the division false.

Is your faith more grounded in what you see and experience or in what you have been told? Refuting the Impossibility of Occurrence at a Time: Razi's Argument
Razi refutes the objection by a divisive argument applied to heaven and earth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Razi refutes the objection that a thing's occurrence at a time is impossible, using a divisive argument that shows both options (identity and addition) lead to absurdity.

Core Idea
Razi applies the objection's own logic to an undeniable case, exposing its invalidity.

The third objection claims that if something occurs at a specific time, its occurrence must be either identical to its essence or additional to it, both impossible. Razi counters by applying the same division to a clear and undeniable case—the occurrence of heaven and earth at this hour—and shows that both alternatives lead to absurdity. This lesson unpacks his argument and its logical structure.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully along with its literal translation. Notice that Razi begins by stating the objection's division and then applies it to a concrete example.
The objection's division is: occurrence either identical to essence or additional.
2
Identify the refutation of the identity option
Razi gives three reasons why occurrence cannot be identical to essence. List these three reasons from the text.
These reasons involve conceivability, relational nature, and temporal consequences.
3
Identify the refutation of the addition option
Find why the addition option leads to infinite regress. How does Razi argue that this option fails?
The additional occurrence would itself require another occurrence, leading to an infinite chain.
4
Understand the conclusion
Conclude that the division itself is invalid because it leads to absurdity in an undeniable case. Ask yourself: what does this imply about the original objection?
Razi shows that the objection's own logic is self-defeating.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب عن السؤال الثالث: أن ذلك التقسيم أيضًا قائم فيما عرف فساده بالضرورة، وذلك لأنه يقال : لو حصل شيء في هذه الساعة لكان حصوله في هذه الساعة إما أن يكون حصوله نفس ذاته أو زائدا على ذاته والقسمان باطلان، فبطل القول بحصوله في هذه الساعة وإنما قلنا : إنه لا يجوز أن يكون حصول هذه السماء وحصول هذه الأرض في هذه الساعة نفس ذات السماء ونفس ذات الأرض لوجوه. أحدها: أنه يمكننا أن نعقل ذات السماء وذات الأرض مع الشك مع حصولهما في هذه الساعة. والثاني : أن حصولهما في هذه الساعة نسبة بين تلك الذاتين إلى هذه الساعة، والنسبة بين الشيئين مغايرة لهما. والثالث : أن ذات السماء والأرض لو كانتا نفس حصولهما في هذه الساعة ففي الساعة الثانية لم يبق حصولهما في الساعة الأولى، فوجب أن لا تبقى ذاتهما في الساعة الثانية، فإن التزموا ذلك وقالوا : الأجسام تحدث حالا بعد حال ألزمناهم في واجب الوجود، وإنما قلنا : إنه لا يجوز أن يكون حصول السماء والأرض في هذه الساعة زائدا على الذات لأن ذلك الزائد يكون حاصلا لا محالة في هذه الساعة، فيكون حصول ذلك الزائد في هذه الساعة زائدا عليه، ويلزم التسلسل وهو محال. فثبت أن ما ذكروه من التقسيم حاصل في هذا المقام الذي عرف بطلانه بالضرورة، فوجب الجزم ببطلان هذا التقسيم.
The answer to the third question: That same division also applies in a context whose corruption is known necessarily. That is because it is said: If something occurs in this hour, its occurrence in this hour is either identical to its essence or additional to its essence, and both divisions are false, so the statement of its occurrence in this hour is invalid. We say that it is not permissible for the occurrence of this heaven and this earth in this hour to be identical to the essence of heaven and the essence of earth, for three reasons. First: we can conceive the essence of heaven and the essence of earth while doubting their occurrence in this hour. Second: their occurrence in this hour is a relationship between those two essences and this hour, and the relationship between two things is distinct from them. Third: if the essences of heaven and earth were identical to their occurrence in this hour, then in the second hour their occurrence in the first hour would no longer remain, so their essences would have to cease in the second hour. If they commit to that and say bodies occur state after state, we would compel them regarding the Necessary of Existence. And we say that it is not permissible for the occurrence of heaven and earth in this hour to be additional to the essence because that additional thing would inevitably occur in this hour, so the occurrence of that additional thing in this hour would be additional to it, leading to infinite regress, which is impossible. Thus it is established that the division they mentioned occurs in this context whose corruption is known necessarily, so one must be certain of the invalidity of this division.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage is an answer to the third objection. The objector used a division: if something occurs at a time, its occurrence is either identical to its essence or additional to it, both claimed impossible. Razi counters by applying the same division to a clear case: the occurrence of heaven and earth at this hour. He shows three reasons why occurrence cannot be identical to essence: (1) we can conceive the essence while doubting the occurrence, so they are distinct; (2) occurrence is a relation, and a relation is distinct from the relata; (3) if identical, then when the occurrence ceases, the essence would cease, which leads to accidents that would force a regress about the Necessary Existent. Then he shows the additional option also fails due to infinite regress. Therefore, the division is invalid because it leads to absurdity in an undeniable case.

Key Terms
حصول
ذات
نسبة
تسلسل
تقسيم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Razi argues that things cannot occur at a time because occurrence is impossible.
Correction: Razi is actually defending the possibility of occurrence; he shows that the objection's own argument is self-defeating by applying it to an undeniable case.

Checkpoint
What is one of the three reasons Razi gives that the occurrence of heaven and earth at this hour cannot be identical to their essence?
A) The essence cannot be conceived separately.
B) The occurrence is a relation distinct from the essences.
C) The essence is eternal.
D) The occurrence cannot be additional.

Key Takeaway
Razi refutes the objection by applying its own division to an undeniable case, showing both options lead to absurdity, thus invalidating the original argument.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever clung to a belief about Allah based on a comfortable assumption, only to find that a careful examination of the evidence (like Razi's rigorous argument) exposes its weakness? What assumption was it, and how will you commit to seeking the truth even if it is uncomfortable?
?
Razi applies a flawed division to an undeniable case to show its absurdity. In your life, are there 'divisions' you impose—false dilemmas between worldly concerns and devotion, or between trust in Allah and personal effort—that prevent you from seeing the harmony in Allah's decree? How can you dismantle these false dichotomies starting today?
?
The objector's argument, if accepted, would deny the very existence of the world. Reflect: Are there any intellectual positions you hold that, if followed to their logical conclusion, would contradict clear truths of the Qur'an or sunnah? What step will you take this week to examine and correct such inconsistencies in your own thinking?

Answer to Objection Four: On Possibility and Preponderance
Razi answers the fourth objection about possibility and preponderance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi resolves the objection about possibility by distinguishing possibility itself from the external factor that tips the balance toward existence or non-existence.

Core Idea
Possibility alone doesn't determine existence; a cause tips the scale.

The fourth objection concerns how possibility (imkan) can be the basis for existence or non-existence. Razi clarifies that possibility pertains to both sides equally, and the actual preponderance comes from an external influencer. This leads to the famous principle: the cause of non‑existence is the non‑existence of the cause.

Guided Path
1
Read the answer carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice that Razi does not dispute the nature of possibility itself, but refocuses on what causes preponderance.
The key phrase: 'لا نزاع في أن الإمكان متعلق بطرفي الوجود والعدم'
2
Identify the two preponderances
Razi explains that preponderance of existence is due to existence of an influencer, and preponderance of non‑existence due to its absence. This is the principle 'علة العدم هي عدم العلة'.
3
Apply the principle
Consider how this refutes the objection: possibility does not necessitate anything; it needs an external cause.
This answer preserves contingency while maintaining causal dependence on God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب عن السؤال الرابع: أنه لا نزاع في أن الإمكان متعلق بطرفي الوجود والعدم، إلا أن رجحان الوجود يكون لوجود ما يؤثر في الوجود، ورجحان العدم يكون لعدم ما يؤثر في الوجود، وهذا هو الكلام المشهور من أن علة العدم هي عدم العلة.

والجواب عن السؤال الخامس: أن عندنا الذات الممكنة حال البقاء تفتقر إلى المبقي لا بمعنى أن المبقي يعطيه حال البقاء وجودًا آخر بل بمعنى أنه ذلك يدوم الوجود الدوام ذلك المؤثر الأول، فلم قلتم بأن ذلك محال؟

والجواب عن السؤال السادس: هو أن الإشكال إنما يعظم إذا قلنا: المؤثر في حدوث الحوادث هو العلة الموجبة بالذات، أما إذا قلنا إنه فاعل مختار اندفع الإشكال لا محالة.

والجواب عن السؤال السابع أن تأثير الشيء في الشيء نسبة مخصوصة بينهما، وقد بينا أن هذه النسبة لا وجود لها في الأعيان، فلم يلزم وقوع التغير في المؤثر. فهذا هو الكلام في هذه المقدمة مع أنه ليس لأحد من المتقدمين ولا من المتأخرين خوض فيها بالتقرير والإشكال وبالله التوفيق.
The answer to the fourth question: There is no dispute that possibility (imkan) pertains to both sides of existence and non-existence, except that the preponderance of existence is due to the existence of something that influences existence, and the preponderance of non-existence is due to the non-existence of something that influences existence. This is the well-known statement that the cause of non-existence is the non-existence of the cause.

The answer to the fifth question: According to us, the contingent essence (al-dhat al-mumkina) in the state of continuance (baqa') is in need of the continuer (al-mubqi) not in the sense that the continuer gives it another existence in the state of continuance, but in the sense that it continues in existence through the continuance of that first influence. So why do you say that is impossible?

The answer to the sixth question: The difficulty only becomes serious if we say that the influencer in the origination of events is the essentially necessitating cause (al-illa al-mujiba bi al-dhat). But if we say that He is a free agent (fa'il mukhtar), the difficulty is necessarily removed.

The answer to the seventh question: The influence of one thing upon another is a specific relation (nisba makhsusa) between them, and we have shown that this relation has no existence in external entities (a'yan), so the occurrence of change in the influencer is not necessitated. This is the discussion of this premise, and there is no one among the earlier or later [scholars] who has delved into it with this exposition and problematization. And with Allah is success.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage contains Imam Razi's answers to four consecutive objections. The fourth answer clarifies that possibility (imkan) does not by itself determine existence or non-existence; rather, the preponderance comes from an external influencer. The famous dictum 'the cause of non-existence is the non-existence of the cause' summarizes this. The fifth answer deals with the continuation of contingent beings: they need a continuer (al-mubqi) not to grant a new existence at each moment, but to sustain the original influence. The sixth answer distinguishes between a necessitating cause and a free agent; the difficulty about causality disappears if we affirm free will (ikhtiyar). The seventh answer argues that causal influence is merely a relation (nisba) with no external reality, so the influencer does not undergo change. Razi concludes that this discussion is unique to him among scholars.

Key Terms
إمكان
رجحان
علة العدم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Possibility itself determines whether something exists or not.
Correction: Possibility is neutral; an external cause tips the balance, as Razi explains.

Checkpoint
According to Razi's answer, what causes the preponderance of existence?
A) The inherent nature of possibility.
B) The existence of something that influences existence.
C) The non-existence of the cause.
D) The essence of the possible being.

Key Takeaway
Possibility does not necessitate; an external cause determines existence or non‑existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you live as if your existence is neutral, or do you recognize that every moment you exist is because God sustains you? What would change if you truly felt that your continuation is not automatic?
?
The principle says non-existence is due to absence of cause. Your faith exists only because God's grace is present. Are you clinging to that cause, or do you assume your faith is self-sustaining? What cause are you neglecting?
?
Razi affirms that possibility alone does not determine outcomes. Are there areas in your life (e.g., character, relationships) where you rely on mere possibility instead of actively seeking the cause that brings good? What concrete step will you take today to seek that cause?

Answer to Objection Five: On the Continuance of Contingents
Razi answers the fifth objection about the need for a continuer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's explanation that a contingent being in a state of continuance needs a continuer not to grant a new existence but to sustain the original creative act.

Core Idea
The continuer sustains the first existence; it does not create a second one.

The fifth objection argues that if contingent beings need a cause to continue existing, then each moment requires a new act of creation. Razi clarifies that the continuer does not give a new existence; rather, the first influence endures, so the need is simply for the preservation of that initial act.

Guided Path
1
Read Razi's answer
Focus on his distinction: the contingent essence in the state of continuance depends on the continuer, but not in the sense of receiving another existence.
Key phrasing: 'لا بمعنى أن المبقي يعطيه حال البقاء وجودًا آخر'
2
Understand the alternative meaning
Razi says the continuance is 'through the continuance of that first influence'. The original creative act keeps the being in existence.
This avoids infinite regress or proliferation of existences.
3
Reflect on the objection
The objection assumes each moment demands a new act. Razi shows it is the same influence continuing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب عن السؤال الرابع: أنه لا نزاع في أن الإمكان متعلق بطرفي الوجود والعدم، إلا أن رجحان الوجود يكون لوجود ما يؤثر في الوجود، ورجحان العدم يكون لعدم ما يؤثر في الوجود، وهذا هو الكلام المشهور من أن علة العدم هي عدم العلة.

?

?
If you truly believed that your existence at this very moment is not a second creation but the continuation of the first, how would that affect your awareness of Allah's presence right now?

Answer to Objection Six: On Free Will vs. Necessitating Cause
Razi answers the sixth objection about causality and free will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the difficulty about causality disappears when we affirm God's free will rather than a necessitating cause.

Core Idea
Free will removes the problem; a necessitating cause creates it.

The sixth objection challenges the notion that God can be the cause of events without necessitating them. Razi points out that the difficulty only arises if we assume God is an essentially necessitating cause. If we affirm that God is a free agent (fa'il mukhtar), the problem dissolves.

Guided Path
1
Read the answer
Notice Razi's clear division: the problem is severe if we hold the view of necessitating cause; it disappears if we hold free will.
Key phrase: 'إنما يعظم إذا قلنا: المؤثر في حدوث الحوادث هو العلة الموجبة بالذات'
2
Distinguish the two views
A necessitating cause produces its effect inevitably; a free agent can choose to act or not.
Razi suggests the objection is only valid against the necessitarian view.
3
Apply to the objection
The objection likely assumed the first view. Razi's answer reframes the discussion around free will, which is the Sunni position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب عن السؤال الرابع: أنه لا نزاع في أن الإمكان متعلق بطرفي الوجود والعدم، إلا أن رجحان الوجود يكون لوجود ما يؤثر في الوجود، ورجحان العدم يكون لعدم ما يؤثر في الوجود، وهذا هو الكلام المشهور من أن علة العدم هي عدم العلة.

Answer to Objection Seven: On Causal Influence as a Relation
Razi answers the seventh objection about the nature of causal influence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's argument that causal influence is merely a relation with no external reality, so the influencer does not change.

Core Idea
Causal influence is just a relation, not a real attribute causing change.

The seventh objection concerns how an unchanging God can cause changing effects. Razi replies that the influence of one thing on another is a specific relation (nisba) that has no existence in external entities. Therefore, no change occurs in the influencer—only the relation changes.

Guided Path
1
Read Razi's answer
Focus on his claim: 'تأثير الشيء في الشيء نسبة مخصوصة بينهما' (influence is a specific relation between them).
He also states this relation has no existence in external entities (a'yan).
2
Understand the implication
If the relation itself has no external reality, then the influencer (God) does not undergo change when the effect occurs. Only the relation (which is a mental consideration) changes.
3
Connect to the objection
The objection assumed that causal influence requires a real attribute in the cause. Razi denies that, so the objection fails.
This is a sophisticated answer rooted in the theory of 'relations have no external existence'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب عن السؤال الرابع: أنه لا نزاع في أن الإمكان متعلق بطرفي الوجود والعدم، إلا أن رجحان الوجود يكون لوجود ما يؤثر في الوجود، ورجحان العدم يكون لعدم ما يؤثر في الوجود، وهذا هو الكلام المشهور من أن علة العدم هي عدم العلة.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Causal influence is a real attribute that changes the cause.
Correction: Razi argues it is merely a relation with no external existence, so the cause remains unchanged.

Checkpoint
According to Razi, why does the influencer not undergo change when it influences?
A) Because the influencer is unchanging by nature.
B) Because influence is a relation that has no existence in external entities.
C) Because influence is an illusion.
D) Because the influencer is passive.

Key Takeaway
Causal influence is a non‑external relation, so the immutable God does not change when creating.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you secretly believe that your actions can 'add' something to God or change His attitude toward you? How does Razi's argument that causal influence is a mere relation with no external reality reshape your understanding of God's immutability?
?
When you pray, do you think of God as being affected or changed by your words? If causal influence is only a relation, what does that mean for how you approach God in worship?
?
Reflect: Have you ever thought that your sin or obedience actually increases or decreases God's essence? Razi says the influencer does not change. How does that challenge your view of divine justice and mercy? What does this teach you about relying on God's unchanging nature rather than your own actions to earn His pleasure?

Critique of the Essential Priority Argument Against Circularity
Al-Razi critiques a flawed argument against circularity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the argument against circularity based on essential priority is problematic and why it fails to prove its point.

Core Idea
Essential priority is either tautological or unexplained; neither helps refute circularity.

Al-Razi begins by examining a common argument against circular causation that relies on the concept of essential priority (al-taqaddum al-dhātī). He shows that this argument is built on a shaky foundation: it assumes a clear notion of priority that is neither temporal nor simply reducible to causation. This lesson walks through his critique, revealing that the argument either begs the question or relies on an undefined concept.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problematic argument
Read the opening lines where the flawed reasoning is presented: the claim that circularity leads to a contradiction based on priority.
2
Understand the nature of priority
Note Al-Razi’s clarification that priority need not be temporal, using the example of the finger and ring.
3
Analyze two possible meanings of 'essential priority'
See how each meaning leads to a dead end—either tautology or lack of clarity.
The two meanings are: priority as effectiveness, or priority as something else.
4
Recognize the conclusion
The argument is ineffective; a better approach is needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة الثالثة: قبل، ومن حيث إنه متأخر يقتضي أن لا يكون موجودًا، وهذا يقتضي أن يكون موجودًا قبل، وأن لا يكون موجودًا، فيلزم اجتماع العدم والوجود في الشيء الواحد من الوجه الواحد، وهو محال. واعلم أن هذه الحجة مبنية على مقدمة مشكلة وهي إثبات التقدم الذاتي، فنقول: ليس المراد من هذا التقدم بالزمان؛ لأنا قد بينا في أول هذا الكتاب أن تقدم المؤثر على الأثر لا يجب أن يكون بالزمان؛ لأن حركة الإصبع علة لحركة الخاتم مع أن هاتين الحركتين يحصلان معاً، ولا تقدم لأحدهما على الأخر بالزمان البتة. وإذا بطل القول بأن المؤثر يجب تقدمه على الأثر بالزمان فنقول: إن عنيت يقولك: المؤثر متقدم على الأثر بالذات كون المؤثر مؤثرًا في الأثر رجع حاصل هذا التقدم إلى التأثير، فقولك: لو كان كل واحد منهما مؤثرًا في الأخر لكان كل واحد منهما متقدما على الآخر مقدمة باطلة؛ لأن تاليها عين مقدمتها من غير فرق، وليس فيها إلا تبديل عبارة بعبارة، فإن كان القول بكون كل واحد منهما مؤثرًا في الآخر معلوم البطلان بالضرورة لم يكن في ذكر هذا الكلام فائدة، ولا إليه حاجة، وإن لم يكن معلوم البطلان بالضرورة لم يكن تغير العبارة مفيدا البتة. وأما إن كان المراد من قوله: المؤثر متقدم بالذات على الأثر أمرًا آخر مغايرا للقدم بالزمان ومغايرا لنفس هذا التأثير فذلك التقدم لا بد من إفادة تصوره، ثم من إقامة الدليل على ثبوته فإن كل واحد من المقامين مما غفلوا عن تلخيصه وتحصيله إلى الآن. والأولى في إبطال الدور أن يقال: المعلول مفتقر إلى العلة، فلو كان كل واحد منهما معلولاً للآخر لكان كل واحد منهما مفتقرًا إلى الآخر، فكان كل واحد منهما مفتقرًا إلى المفتقر إلى نفسه فيلزم كون كل واحد منهما مفتقرًا إلى نفسه، وذلك محال، لأن الافتقار إلى الشيء إضافة بين المفتقر والمفتقر إليه، والإضافة لا تعقل إلا بين الشيئين. فإن قال قائل: الإضافيان كل واحد منهما علة لوجود الآخر، وذلك لأنه يلزم من فرض وجود أيهما كان وجود الآخر قطعاً، ومن فرض عدم أيهما كان عدم الآخر قطعاً، فوجب كون كل واحد منهما علة لوجود الآخر. فالجواب: إن قلنا: إن الإضافات لا وجود لها في الأعيان فقد زال السؤال، وإن قلنا: إن لها وجودًا في الأعيان قلنا: الملازمة بينهما معللة بوحدة السبب.
The third question: [It is said] 'before, and insofar as it is posterior, it necessitates that it not exist, before, and this necessitates that it exist before, and that it not exist, before, so there follows the conjunction of non-existence and existence in one thing from one aspect, which is impossible.' Know that this argument is based on a problematic premise, namely the affirmation of essential priority. We say: what is meant by this priority is not temporal; for we have shown at the beginning of this book that the priority of the cause over the effect need not be temporal, because the movement of the finger is the cause of the movement of the ring, even though these two movements occur together, and there is no temporal priority of one over the other at all. Since the statement that the cause must be temporally prior to the effect is refuted, we say: If by your saying 'the cause is essentially prior to the effect' you mean that the cause is effective in the effect, then the content of this priority reduces to the effect itself. So your saying, 'If each of them were effective in the other, then each would be prior to the other' is a false premise, because its consequent is identical to its antecedent with no difference; there is nothing in it except the substitution of one expression for another. If the statement that each of them is effective in the other is known to be false necessarily, then there is no benefit in mentioning this speech, nor any need for it; and if it is not known to be false necessarily, then changing the expression is not at all beneficial. But if what is meant by his saying 'the cause is essentially prior to the effect' is something else, different from temporal priority and different from this effectiveness itself, then that priority must be conceptualized and then a proof must be established for it; for each of these two stations—conceptualization and proof—they have neglected to summarize and attain until now. The better way to refute circularity is to say: The effect depends upon the cause. So if each of them were an effect of the other, then each would depend upon the other; thus each would depend upon that which depends upon itself, which entails that each depends upon itself. That is impossible, because dependence upon something is a relation (idāfa) between the dependent and the depended-upon, and a relation is inconceivable except between two things. If someone says: The two relatives (al-iḍāfiyyān) are each a cause of the existence of the other—because from the assumption of the existence of either of them, the existence of the other necessarily follows, and from the assumption of the non-existence of either of them, the non-existence of the other necessarily follows—so each must be a cause of the existence of the other. The answer: If we say that relations have no existence in external entities, then the question ceases; and if we say that they have existence in external entities, we say the entailment between them is grounded in the unity of the cause.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of circularity (dawr) in causal chains. Al-Razi begins by critiquing a previous argument that attempted to prove the impossibility of circularity by appealing to essential priority (al-taqaddum al-dhātī). He points out that this argument is problematic because it relies on an unclear notion of priority. He first shows that priority need not be temporal, using the example of the finger and the ring moving simultaneously. Then he argues that if 'essential priority' just means 'being effective', then the argument reduces to tautology. If it means something else, it must first be clarified and then proved. Al-Razi then presents a sounder proof: the effect depends on its cause; if each of two things were an effect of the other, each would depend on the other, leading to each depending on itself—an impossibility because dependence is a relation and requires two distinct relata. He then addresses an objection: what if the two things are relative terms (al-iḍāfiyyān) that are mutually entailing? The answer is that either relations have no real existence (so the objection is void) or, if they do, the mutual entailment is explained by the unity of the cause (like the relation of paternity and sonship both depending on the same reality). Thus the proof against circularity stands.

Key Terms
دور
تقدم ذاتي
تأثير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Causal priority always implies temporal priority.
Correction: Al-Razi gives the example of finger and ring moving simultaneously to show that cause can be simultaneous with effect.

Checkpoint
What does Al-Razi identify as the problem with the argument against circularity that relies on essential priority?
A) It assumes temporal priority is necessary.
B) The concept of essential priority is either tautological or undefined.
C) The argument is too complex to understand.
D) It uses a false analogy.

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi shows that the common argument against circularity based on essential priority is either tautological or relies on an undefined concept, thus it is unsound.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever defended a belief using an argument that, upon deeper inspection, turned out to be circular or tautological? Are you willing to re-examine your own convictions with the same intellectual rigor Al-Razi applies here?
?
Al-Razi points out that an undefined concept cannot be used as a premise. In your own understanding of Islamic theology, are there terms you use without fully understanding their meaning? What would it cost you to clarify them, and are you prepared to pay that price?
?
This lesson shows that even seemingly strong arguments can collapse when their foundational premises are examined. Are you prepared to let go of arguments that are convenient for your position if they are not sound? What does that say about your commitment to truth over comfort?

A Sound Proof of the Impossibility of Circular Causality
Al-Razi provides a sound proof against circularity and addresses an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Razi's correct proof against circular causation using the concept of dependence (iftiqār) and his response to the objection about relational causality.

Core Idea
Circular causality is impossible because it makes a thing depend on itself, which violates the nature of dependence.

After critiquing flawed arguments, Al-Razi presents what he considers the better way to refute circularity: by appealing to the notion of dependence (iftiqār). He argues that if each of two things depends on the other, each would end up depending on itself, which is impossible because dependence is a relation between two distinct entities. He then addresses an objection involving relational terms (al-iḍāfiyyān) and shows that it does not undermine his proof.

Guided Path
1
Understand the better proof
Read the core argument starting from 'والأولى في إبطال الدور أن يقال' and note how Al-Razi uses the concept of dependence.
2
Grasp the logic
Trace how mutual dependence leads to self-dependence, and why self-dependence is absurd because dependence is a relation between two distinct things.
3
Consider the objection
Read the objection: what if the two things are relational terms that imply each other's existence?
4
Examine the answer
Al-Razi gives two responses: either relations have no real existence (so the objection is moot) or they share a common cause.

Source Text

Causality and Created Things

The cause must exist with its effect
Al-Razi proves the simultaneous existence of the complete efficient cause and its effect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the efficient cause must coexist with its effect, based on Al-Razi's proof and refutation of the temporal gap objection.

Core Idea
The effect cannot exist without its cause existing at the same moment.

This passage presents a key premise in Al-Razi's proof for God's existence: the efficient cause must be simultaneous with its effect. Before tackling infinite regress, Al-Razi establishes that if a cause produces an effect, the cause must exist when the effect comes into being. He then anticipates and refutes the objection that the effect could be delayed.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Al-Razi uses a very compressed style here.
2
Identify the core claim and proof
Find the premise that the efficient cause must exist at the moment of the effect. Then follow the proof by contradiction: what happens if the cause is absent at the time of effect?
The proof assumes the cause is assumed to be the cause of the effect.
3
Analyze the objection and refutation
Read the objection: could the cause produce an effect after it ceases? Then trace Al-Razi's two-part refutation based on the nature of 'necessitation' (ījāb).
The refutation avoids infinite regress by showing that if ījāb is distinct, it leads to an infinite chain.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقدمة الرابعة من مقدمات برهان إثبات العلم بواجب الوجود: إبطال للتسلسل : واعلم أنا قبل الخوض في تقرير هذا المطلوب نفتقر إلى تقديم مقدمة وهي أن العلة المؤثرة لا بد وأن تكون موجودة حال وجود المعلول، والدليل عليه أنه لو لم يكن كذلك لكان عند حصول المعلول تكون العلة غير موجودة فيلزم حصول المعلول حال عدم العلة، فحينئذ يكون حصول ذلك المعلول لا لأجل وجود تلك العلة، وقد فرضنا الأمر كذلك هذا خلف. لا يقال : لم لا يجوز أن يقال: العلة في حال وجودها توجب وجود المعلول بعد انقضاء العلة، وعلى هذا التقدير يكون وجود المعلول معللا بتلك العلة التي كانت موجودة قبل ذلك؟ لأنا نقول : القول بأن هذه العلة أوجبت في هذه الساعة حصول المعلول غدا: قول باطل، وذلك لأن هذه العلة لما صدق عليها في هذه الساعة أنها أوجبت ذلك المعلول فإيجاب ذلك المعلول إما أن يكون عبارة عن حدوث ذلك المعلول أو عن شيء آخر يترتب عليه حدوث ذلك المعلول، فإن كان الأول لزم حدوث ذلك المعلول في هذه الساعة لا بعده، وذلك لأنه لما صدق على تلك العلة أوجبت في هذه الساعة ذلك المعلول، وهذا الإيجاب عبارة عن حدوث ذلك المعلول، ولما وجد ذلك الإيجاب في هذه الساعة لزم حصول ذلك المعلول في هذه الساعة، فالقول بأن ذلك المعلول يحصل لا في هذه الساعة بل في الساعة الثانية قول يناقض الكلام الأول. وأما إن قلنا بأن إيجاب العلة لذلك المعلول عبارة عن أمر مغاير لذلك المعلول، ويترتب عليه ذلك المعلول، فهذا باطل ؛ لأن ذلك المغاير لابد وأن يصدق عليه أنه يوجب في الساعة ذلك المعلول في هذه الساعة الثانية فيكون إيجابه لذلك المعلول زائدا على ذاته ويلزم التسلسل في الإيجابات، وكل ذلك محال، فثبت بما ذكرنا أن المؤثر التام لا بد وأن يوجد الأثر معه.
The fourth premise among the premises of the proof for establishing knowledge of the Necessary Existent: the refutation of infinite regress. Know that before delving into the establishment of this claim we need to present a premise, namely that the efficient cause must exist at the moment of the existence of the effect. The proof for it is that if it were not so, then at the occurrence of the effect the cause would be non-existent, and so the occurrence of the effect would necessarily be at the non-existence of the cause. Then the occurrence of that effect would not be due to the existence of that cause, and we had assumed the matter to be such—this is a contradiction. Let it not be said: Why is it not permissible to say that the cause, during its existence, necessitates the existence of the effect after the passing away of the cause, and on this assumption the existence of the effect is caused by that cause which existed before? For we say: The statement that this cause at this hour necessitates the occurrence of the effect tomorrow is a false statement, because when this cause is truly described at this hour as necessitating that effect, then the necessitation (ījāb) of that effect is either an expression for the coming-to-be (ḥudūth) of that effect, or for something else upon which the coming-to-be of that effect follows. If it is the first, then the coming-to-be of that effect necessarily occurs at this hour, not after it—because when that cause is truly described as necessitating at this hour that effect, and this necessitation is an expression for the coming-to-be of that effect, and since that necessitation exists at this hour, the occurrence of that effect at this hour is necessary. So the statement that that effect occurs not at this hour but at the second hour is a statement that contradicts the first statement. But if we say that the cause's necessitation of that effect is an expression for something distinct from that effect, and that effect follows upon it, this is false—because that distinct thing must be truly described as necessitating at that hour that effect at this second hour, so its necessitation of that effect would be additional to its essence, and an infinite regress (tasalsul) of necessitations would follow. All of that is impossible. So it is established by what we have mentioned that the complete cause must exist together with its effect.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage is a self-contained proof of the fourth premise needed for the argument for God's existence: the efficient cause must coexist with its effect. Al-Razi presents a proof by contradiction: if the cause did not exist when the effect occurs, the effect would exist without its cause, contradicting the assumption that it is caused. He then anticipates an objection: could the cause produce an effect after it ceases to exist? He refutes this by analyzing the notion of 'necessitation' (ījāb). If the cause's act of necessitation is the same as the effect's coming-to-be, then the effect must occur at the same time. If the necessitation is something else on which the effect follows, then that something else would itself need another act of necessitation, leading to an infinite regress of necessitations. Thus, the only coherent position is that the complete cause and its effect are simultaneous. This premise is crucial for the subsequent proof against infinite regress.

Key Terms
علة مؤثرة
إيجاب
تسلسل
حدوث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Al-Razi is arguing for temporal simultaneity in all causal relationships, meaning cause and effect always occur at the same time.
Correction: Al-Razi's focus is on the logical necessity that the effect cannot exist without its cause existing at that moment; the argument is about the complete efficient cause, not about temporal priority in all cases.

Checkpoint
How does Al-Razi refute the objection that a cause could produce an effect after it ceases to exist?
A) By asserting that the cause must be eternal.
B) By showing that such a scenario leads to an infinite regress of necessitations.
C) By stating that the effect is always delayed.
D) By appealing to divine power.

Key Takeaway
The complete efficient cause and its effect must exist together; an effect cannot come to be after its cause has ceased.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that your very existence at this moment is directly caused by Allah's continuous existence, not merely by past events? If so, why do you often feel secure in your own strength or forget that you are dependent on Him every instant?
?
If the cause must exist with the effect, then your faith (īmān) must be present and active right now to be real. Is your īmān currently alive, or are you relying on a past profession of faith without renewing it? What will you do to ensure your cause (the means of īmān) is present today?
?
The objection that a cause can produce an effect later is attractive because it allows us to think we can 'store up' spiritual deeds. But Al-Razi shows that the effect (your reward or state) cannot be separated from the cause (your action and intention in the present). Are you deceiving yourself by thinking that a past good deed will automatically benefit you without a present connection to Allah? What will you change?

Cause and Effect Must Be Simultaneous
Razi argues for the simultaneity of cause and effect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Razi argues that an efficient cause must coexist with its effect, and how he refutes the objection that a cause can necessitate a delayed effect.

Core Idea
A true cause must be present at the same time as its effect.

Imam Razi sets up a crucial preliminary for his proof against infinite regress. He establishes that a cause cannot exist and then later produce an effect after it ceases. This principle is essential for understanding the nature of divine causality and the refutation of infinite chains. In this passage, he provides a logical demonstration and answers a potential objection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing it. Then read the literal translation. Let the author's own argument come through before you interpret.
Notice that Razi uses a compressed logical style.
2
Identify the main claim and proof
The passage claims that the effect must exist simultaneously with the cause. The proof is by contradiction: if the cause were absent at the time of the effect, the effect would be uncaused.
This is the direct argument.
3
Examine the objection
The objection asks: why can't the cause, while existing, necessitate an effect that occurs later? Understand the objection before proceeding to Razi's answer.
This is a natural question to ask.
4
Analyze Razi's two-part response
Razi breaks down the meaning of 'necessitation' (ijab). First, if it is identical to the effect, the effect must occur immediately. Second, if it is something else, that something would itself require a further necessitation, leading to infinite regress.
Each case is treated separately.
5
Conclude the principle
Having refuted the objection, Razi concludes that the complete efficient cause must coexist with its effect. Reflect on why this principle is foundational for arguments against infinite regress.
The conclusion is explicit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقدمة الرابعة من مقدمات برهان إثبات العلم بواجب الوجود: إبطال التسلسل واعلم أنا قبل الخوض في تقرير هذا المطلوب نفتقر إلى تقديم مقدمة وهي أن العلة المؤثرة لا بد وأن تكون موجودة حال وجود المعلول، والدليل عليه أنه لو لم يكن كذلك لكان عند حصول المعلول تكون العلة غير موجودة فيلزم حصول المعلول حال عدم العلة، فحينئذ يكون حصول ذلك المعلول لا لأجل وجود تلك العلة، وقد فرضنا الأمر كذلك هذا خلف. لا يقال: لم لا يجوز أن يقال: العلة في حال وجودها توجب وجود المعلول بعد انقضاء العلة، وعلى هذا التقدير يكون وجود المعلول معللا بتلك العلة التي كانت موجودة قبل ذلك؟ لأنا نقول: القول بأن هذه العلة أوجبت في هذه الساعة حصول المعلول غدا: قول باطل، وذلك لأن هذه العلة لما صدق عليها في هذه الساعة أنها أوجبت ذلك المعلول فإيجاب ذلك المعلول إما أن يكون عبارة عن حدوث ذلك المعلول أو عن شيء آخر يترتب عليه حدوث ذلك المعلول، فإن كان الأول لزم حدوث ذلك المعلول في هذه الساعة لا بعده، وذلك لأنه لما صدق على تلك العلة أوجبت في هذه الساعة ذلك المعلول، وهذا الإيجاب عبارة عن حدوث ذلك المعلول، ولما وجد ذلك الإيجاب في هذه الساعة لزم حصول ذلك المعلول في هذه الساعة، فالقول بأن ذلك المعلول يحصل لا في هذه الساعة بل في الساعة الثانية قول يناقض الكلام الأول. وأما إن قلنا بأن إيجاب العلة لذلك المعلول عبارة عن أمر مغاير لذلك المعلول، ويترتب عليه ذلك المعلول، فهذا باطل؛ لأن ذلك المغاير لابد وأن يصدق عليه أنه يوجب في الساعة ذلك المعلول في هذه الساعة الثانية فيكون إيجابه لذلك المعلول زائدا على ذاته ويلزم التسلسل في الإيجابات، وكل ذلك محال، فثبت بما ذكرنا أن المؤثر التام لا بد وأن يوجد الأثر معه.
The Fourth Preliminary from the Preliminaries of the Proof of Knowledge of the Necessary Existent: The Refutation of Infinite Regress. Know that before delving into the exposition of this sought-after [proposition], we need to present a preliminary, namely that the effective cause must necessarily exist at the time of the effect's existence. The proof of this is that if it were not so, then at the occurrence of the effect, the cause would be non-existent, and thus the occurrence of the effect in a state of the absence of the cause would be necessary. Then that effect would occur not because of that cause's existence, and we had assumed it to be so; this is a contradiction. It should not be said: 'Why is it not permissible to say: the cause, in its state of existence, necessitates the existence of the effect after the cessation of the cause, and on this estimation the effect's existence would be caused by that cause which existed previously?' For we say: The statement that this cause necessitated at this hour the occurrence of the effect tomorrow is a false statement, because when this cause is truly described at this hour as necessitating that effect, then the necessitation of that effect is either an expression of the occurrence of that effect or of something else upon which the occurrence of that effect depends. If the first, then the occurrence of that effect in this hour would be necessary, not after it, because when that cause is truly described as having necessitated in this hour that effect, and this necessitation is an expression of the occurrence of that effect, and when that necessitation existed in this hour, the occurrence of that effect in this hour is necessary. So the statement that that effect occurs not in this hour but in the second hour is a statement contradicting the first statement. And if we say that the cause's necessitation of that effect is an expression of something other than that effect, and that effect depends upon it, then this is false, because that something else must be truly described as necessitating in that hour that effect in the second hour, so its necessitation of that effect would be additional to its essence and leads to infinite regress in necessitations, and all of that is impossible. So it is established by what we have mentioned that the complete efficient cause must exist together with its effect.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage is a preliminary (muqaddima) establishing a crucial principle for the subsequent proofs against infinite regress. Imam Razi argues that an efficient cause must be present at the same time as its effect. He first gives a proof: if the cause were absent when the effect occurs, the effect would exist without a cause, contradicting the assumption that it has a cause. Then he considers an objection: could the cause, while existing, necessitate an effect that occurs later, after the cause has ceased? He answers this in two steps. First, if 'necessitation' is identical with the occurrence of the effect, then the effect must occur immediately, not later; claiming a delay contradicts the idea that the cause necessitated now. Second, if 'necessitation' is something else that later produces the effect, then that something else would itself need a further necessitation to produce the effect at the later time, leading to an infinite regress of necessitations, which is impossible. Thus he concludes that the complete cause (al-mu'aththir al-tamm) must coexist with its effect (al-athar).

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A cause can exist and then later produce an effect after the cause has ceased.
Correction: Razi demonstrates that such a scenario either makes the effect simultaneous with the cause (if the necessitation is the effect itself) or leads to an infinite regress of necessitations (if the necessitation is something separate). Hence, the cause must coexist with its effect.

C) Because the effect would be uncaused.
D) Both A and B.

Key Takeaway
Imam Razi demonstrates that the complete efficient cause must be simultaneous with its effect; otherwise, either the effect would be uncaused or an infinite regress of necessitations would arise.

?
The objection Razi refutes suggests that a cause can necessitate an effect after it ceases. Is there a part of your spiritual life where you assume past obedience guarantees future benefit without present effort? How does Razi's argument force you to reconsider that assumption?

Why There Must Be a First Cause
Razi disproves infinite regress by analyzing two possibilities, concluding a necessary first cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi's argument against infinite regress demonstrates that any chain of causes must end with a being that is necessary in itself.

Core Idea
Infinite regress leads to contradiction; a necessary first cause is unavoidable.

Razi presents a logical argument that any chain of causes must have a beginning. He considers two scenarios for an infinite sequence, showing both lead to impossibility unless the chain ends with a being that is necessary in itself. This lesson unpacks that reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get the feel of the original. Then read the literal translation. Notice the key terms like 'incomplete' and 'increased' sequences.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Understand the two possibilities
Razi examines two cases: an incomplete sequence with no beginning, and a sequence that is cut off at the last end. Identify these in the text.
3
Follow the absurdity of the first possibility
If the incomplete sequence has no beginning, the whole equals the part—an impossibility. See why that is self-contradictory.
4
Analyze the second possibility and its consequence
If the sequence is cut off at the end, it becomes finite. Then that end must be either possible in itself or necessary. Trace the logic to its conclusion.
5
Conclude: the necessary first cause
The end cannot be possible because it would need another cause. So it must be necessary in itself, which is exactly what the argument sought to prove.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الناقصة لا إلى بداية، فيكون الكل مثل البعض، وذلك محال - وإما أن تنقطع الجملة الناقصة من الطرف الأخير، فتكون الجملة الناقصة متناهية من ذلك الطرف، والزائدة زادت عليها بأربعة فتكون الجملة الزائدة أيضًا متناهية من ذلك الطرف، فيكون للأسباب والمسببات في سلمة التصاعد طرف ومبدأ، وذلك يمنع من القول بأنه لا نهاية لها، ثم ذلك الطرف إن كان ممكنا لذاته افتقر إلى مؤثر آخر فلم يكن طرفاً، هذا خلف، وإن كان واجبًا لذاته فذلك هو المطلوب
The incomplete (sequence) has no beginning, so the whole would be like the part, and that is impossible. Or the incomplete sequence is cut off at the last end, so the incomplete sequence is finite from that end, and the increased (sequence) is increased by four, so the increased sequence is also finite from that end. Thus for causes and effects in the ascending ladder there is an end and a beginning, and that prevents the statement that it has no end. Then that end: if it is possible in itself, it needs another effect, so it would not be an end; this is a contradiction. And if it is necessary in itself, then that is the sought.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage is a proof against infinite regress (tasalsul). Razi presents two scenarios. First, if the incomplete infinite sequence has no beginning, then the whole equals the part, which is impossible. Second, if the sequence is cut off at one end, it becomes finite. Then that finite end must be either possible or necessary. If possible, it needs a cause, contradicting its being the end. If necessary, we have reached the necessary being. The argument forces acceptance of a first cause that is necessary in itself.

Key Terms

ناقصة (incomplete)
زائدة (increased)
طرف (end)
مبدأ (beginning)
ممكن لذاته (possible in itself)
واجب لذاته (necessary in itself)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Infinite regress of causes is possible and does not lead to contradiction.
Correction: Razi's argument shows that an infinite regress leads to logical contradictions, such as the whole equaling the part or the impossibility of a chain without an end. Therefore, a first cause that is necessary in itself must exist.

Checkpoint

B) It must be necessary in itself
C) It is possible in itself
D) It is infinite

Key Takeaway
The argument proves that an infinite chain of causes is impossible, necessitating a first cause that is necessary in itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

?
When you consider the ultimate reason for your existence, do you find yourself trapped in a chain of 'I do this because...' that never ends? How does this argument force you to stop and admit that only a necessary being can be the final answer, and how should that change your attitude today?

Equality of Accidental Qualities Across Species Individuals
Razi proves equality of accidental qualities across species individuals and applies to celestial spheres.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's argument that individuals of the same species share the same accidental qualities, and how this applies to celestial bodies, challenging the notion of their immutability.

Core Idea
If an accidental quality is essential, it must apply to all individuals of the same species.

Razi tackles a crucial question: do individuals of the same species differ in their accidental qualities? He argues that what is truly accidental cannot be tied to particularization, and this has profound implications for the celestial spheres. In this passage, he presents a logical proof, anticipates an objection, and applies his reasoning to the heavens.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then the English translation. Let the structure emerge naturally.
Pay attention to the technical terms: qābilīya, māhīya, lāzim, ʿāriḍ, taʿayyun.
2
Identify the main claim and the two branches
The proof starts with a conditional: if the quality is a necessary concomitant of the essence, it applies equally; if not, it leads to infinite regress or a necessary base. Note how this establishes the conclusion.
3
Understand the objection about particularization
The objector argues that individuals differ in their particularization (taʿayyun), which could affect the quality. Read the objection carefully and Razi's two-part answer.
Two views on particularization: non-existent (ʿadamī) or existent (thubūtī).
4
Apply the conclusion to celestial spheres
Razi concludes that celestial bodies are like elements in being subject to change. Identify the examples he gives (perforation, transformation, etc.) and the significance for theology.
This premise is beneficial for understanding the Creator and the Resurrection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة الثالثة
وذلك لأن قابلية هذا العرض إن كانت من لوازم تلك الماهية فإذا حصلت تلك الماهية لزم حصول تلك القابلية، فوجب أن يصح على كل واحد منها ما صح على واحد منها، وإن لم يكن من لوازمها كان من عوارضها، فيعود الكلام في قبلية تلك القابلية؛ فإن كانت أيضًا من العوارض يلزم إما التسلسل وإما الانتهاء إلى قابلية لازمة لتلك الماهية وحينئذ يحصل المطلوب.
فإن قال قائل : أفراد النوع الواحد وإن كانت متساوية في ماهية ذلك النوع لكنها غير متساوية في كون كل واحد منها غير ذلك الشخص، وذلك المعين، وذلك لأن تعين هذا إن كان حاصلا لذلك فهذا هو عين ذاك، فلم يكن مغايرا له قثبت أ[؟] تعين كل واحد من الأفراد غير حاصل للفرد الآخر.
وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول : لم لا يجوز أن يكون ذلك التعين شرطا لتلك القابلية في هذا الفرد أو يكون تعين الفرد الآخر مانعا من هذه القابلية، وإذا كان الأمر كذلك لم يلزم أن يصح على كل واحد من أفراد النوع الواحد ما صح على فرد من أفراده. والجواب : أما على قول من يقول : التعين أمر عدمي فالسؤال ساقط، وأما عند من يقول إنه أمر ثبوتي فجوابه : أن ذلك التعين ليس من لوازم تلك الماهية، وإلا لزم أن يكون ذلك النوع في ذلك الشخص، لكنه ليس الأمر كذلك ؛ لأن هذا الكلام مفروض في نوع حصل له أفراد كثير بالفعل، فإذن ذلك التعين الذي به صار ذلك الشخص ذلك المعين أمر غير لازم لتلك الماهية ، فهو عارض جائز الزوال، وكل ما كان عارضا لذلك الشخص بسبب ذلك التعين وجب أيضًا أن يكون جائز الزوال، وذلك يقتضي أن يكون اتصاف كل واحد من الأجسام بما اتصف به أمرًا ممكنا جائزا .
وعند هذا ظهر أن كل ما على العناصر فمثله على الأفلاك، فكان الخرق والالتئام والفطور والانشقاق جائزا على الأفلاك، وكما يمكن انقلاب الأرض ماء والماء هواء والهواء نارًا فكذلك يمكن انقلاب الفلك أرضًا والأرض فلكاً، وكما يمكن كون الفلك محيطا بالأرض والأرض مركزاً، فكذلك يمكن انقلاب كون الأرض محيطا والفلك مركزاً، وهذه المقدمة كما أنها عظيمة المنفعة في معرفة المبدأ فهي أيضًا عظيمة المنفعة في معرفة المعاد، وتصحيح ما ورد في القرآن من أحوال القيامة.
The third issue: And that is because the receptivity (qābilīya) of this accident, if it is among the necessary concomitants (lawāzim) of that essence (māhīya), then when that essence occurs, the occurrence of that receptivity is necessary, so it must be valid for each one of them what is valid for one of them. And if it is not among its necessary concomitants, it is among its accidents (ʿawāriḍ). Then the discussion returns to the priority of that receptivity; if it also is among the accidents, then either infinite regress (tasalsul) follows or ending at a receptivity that is necessary for that essence, and then the desired result is obtained. If someone says: The individuals of a single species, even if they are equal in the essence of that species, they are not equal in the fact that each one is other than that person and that particular; and that is because the particularization (taʿayyun) of this, if it occurs to that, then it is identical to that, so it is not different from it. [Then] it is established that the particularization of each individual is not obtained for the other individual. And when this is established, we say: Why is it not permissible that that particularization be a condition for that receptivity in this individual, or that the particularization of the other individual be a hindrance to this receptivity? And if the matter is such, then it does not follow that what is valid for one individual of a species is valid for every one of its individuals. The answer: As for the view of the one who says that particularization is a non-existent (ʿadamī) matter, the question is dropped. As for the one who says it is an existent (thubūtī) matter, the answer is: That particularization is not among the necessary concomitants of that essence; otherwise it would follow that that species is in that person, but it is not so; because this discourse is assumed for a species that actually has many individuals. So then, that particularization by which that person became that particular is not necessary for that essence, so it is an accident liable to perish (jāʾiz al-zawāl). And everything that is accidental to that person due to that particularization must also be liable to perish. And that requires that the qualification of each body with what it is qualified by is possible and permissible. And at this point it appears that whatever applies to the elements (al-ʿanāṣir) applies likewise to the celestial spheres (al-aflāk). So perforation (al-kharq), mending (al-iltiʾām), fissures (al-fuṭūr), and splitting (al-inshiqāq) are permissible regarding the celestial spheres. And just as it is possible for earth to turn into water, water into air, and air into fire, likewise it is possible for a sphere to turn into earth and earth into a sphere. And just as it is possible for the sphere to encompass the earth and the earth to be the center, likewise it is possible for the earth to encompass and the sphere to be the center. And this premise, as it is of great benefit in knowledge of the Beginning (al-mabdaʾ), is also of great benefit in knowledge of the Resurrection (al-maʿād), and in verifying what has come in the Qur'an about the states of the Day of Resurrection.
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage presents a proof followed by an objection and answer, then an application to celestial bodies. It begins by stating the third issue: If a certain accidental quality (receptivity) is a necessary concomitant of an essence, then whenever that essence exists, that quality must exist in all individuals of that species. If not a necessary concomitant, it is an accident; then the discussion turns to the series of accidents. The objector argues that individuals of the same species differ in their particularization (taʿayyun), which could affect the presence of the quality. The answer distinguishes two views: if particularization is non-existent, the objection fails; if it is an existent accident, it is not essential to the essence, so it is merely accidental and perishable, thus the quality remains equally applicable. The conclusion is that qualities that apply to the four elements also apply to the celestial spheres, making events like perforation, mending, and transformation possible for the heavens. This premise is useful for understanding the Creator and the Resurrection as described in the Quran.

جائز الزوال

خرق
التئام
